Important News

State Funeral Held for the Late President Tan 63

After the death of the late President Tan Yankai, his body was temporarily placed in the First Park. Now that the construction of his tomb is largely complete, a state funeral was held on September 4th. The State Funeral Preparatory Office meticulously planned all the ceremonies according to the State Funeral Law. Many important figures from the central government and leaders from all sectors of the country, as well as foreign guests, either came to Nanjing in person or sent representatives to participate. On that day, all civil servants wore black armbands, and all entertainment was suspended. All government agencies, organizations, businesses, and residences flew flags at half-mast. The ceremony was solemn and respectful. The details of the funeral are described below:

▲ A Glimpse of the Funeral Hall: A new white mourning archway was erected at the First Park. Gifts such as newly received wreaths and framed inscriptions were displayed throughout the funeral hall. The State Funeral Preparatory Office assigned various personnel to handle all matters related to the transfer of the coffin and the funeral rites. Several inspectors led party members and Boy Scouts to maintain order. Military and police forces were deployed to maintain security inside and outside the venue.

▲ Funeral Arrangements: From the First Park to the cemetery, all rugged, low-lying, and waterlogged sections of the road were repaired and leveled. Wooden signs were placed along both sides of the road, adorned with party and national flags and the words "State Funeral of President Tan," to mark the route. The coffin cover was made of blue satin and trimmed with white silk tassels. The coffin was draped with an embroidered national emblem. The high carrying poles, specially made and lacquered in vermilion, were decorated with blue satin. The carrying poles were topped with party emblems. The pallbearers were hired from Hunan Province and wore neat uniforms of blue cloth with white trim. The hearse was provided by the Shanghai International Funeral Parlor, painted in black enamel and lined with blue satin and white silk tassels. At the start of the procession, the coffin was carried by pallbearers to the gate, then placed on the hearse and transported slowly to the cemetery. It was then carried by pallbearers to the burial chamber for interment.

▲ Central Government's Offering: At 4:30 AM, Dai Chuanxian, a standing committee member of the Central Party Headquarters, was specially dispatched to offer sacrifices before the coffin. His eulogy read: "Alas, President Tan, your life was the hope of the nation, your death the sorrow of the world. Only 357 days have passed since your passing, yet your merits and virtues have become increasingly difficult to emulate. In times of national difficulty, who would not eagerly seek to contribute, or wander on the wrong path, or rush about in confusion? You alone remained calm and composed, neither radical nor submissive, like rain and dew nourishing all things without being seen, like great rivers and mountains benefiting people without their knowledge. Now that we have lost our guide, where shall the people turn? How shall the nation be governed? Alas, you are now buried deep in the earth. We erect a tall ornamental column, plant a field of grass. Though mountains and rivers may fade, and you long knew this, we honor your virtues and merits with the highest honors of a state funeral, so that even centuries later, people will still admire and learn from you. We offer this sacrifice."

▲ Transfer of the Coffin Ceremony: At 5:00 AM, Central Executive and Supervisory Committee members, the Chairman of the National Government, heads of various Yuan and departments, members of the State Funeral Committee, including Yu Youren, Dai Chuanxian, Ding Weifen, Wu Jingheng, Shao Yuanchong, Song Ziwen, Ye Chucang, Zhu Pei, De Wang Zhengting, Wang Boqun, Zhang Qun, Jiao Yitang, Zhu Jiahua, Zeng Yangfu, Wang Boling, Chen Lifu, Chen Zhaoying, Kexing'e, Miao Peicheng, Lian Shenghai, Chen Yi, Ma Fuxiang, Zhang Wohua, Li Shuhua, Niu Yongjian, Zhang Zhijiang, Zheng Hongnian, Jiang Zuobin, Lu Dipng, Wei Daoming, He Yaozu, Ru Yuli, and Lin Xiang, as well as leaders or representatives from provincial and municipal party, government, and military organizations, gathered at the First Park to hold the ceremony for the transfer of the coffin. Yu Youren presided over the ceremony, which included the following: (1) Stand at attention (2) Play mournful music (3) Offer flowers (4) Read the eulogy (5) Observe a moment of silence (6) Bow three times (7) Play mournful music (8) Transfer the coffin.

▲ Announcement of the Transfer: "On this fourth day of September in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government, the heads of the five Yuan, ministers of various departments, and chairmen of various committees, announce to the spirit of the late President Tan Yankai: The government respectfully follows the established rules and will hold a state funeral for you today, September 4th, at the foot of Zijin Mountain. We respectfully lead the officials, soldiers, civilians, and elders in carrying out this solemn event. Soft carriages carry the procession, mindful not to cause any disturbance. We respectfully offer incense and flowers and humbly request your acceptance. We respectfully announce that the blue sky and white sun will forever remember your contributions as a pillar of the nation, and the land of dragons and tigers will forever protect your resting place."

▲ Temporary Traffic Control: From 4:00 AM, traffic on the northern section of Gongyuan Road and the four alleys of Fucheng Bridge and Changfu Street was temporarily suspended. All vehicles participating in the ceremony arriving at the First Park were rerouted via Zhongzheng Street and Dazhong Bridge after 4:00 AM. Those heading to the cemetery were rerouted via Dazhong Bridge, Zhongzheng Street, Taiping Road, Yanggongjing, Erlangmiao, and Zhongshan Road, exiting through Zhongshan Gate, but only until 5:00 AM. Vehicles were not permitted to pass through the section of road beyond Zhongshan Gate after that time.

▲ Funeral Procession: Military police and band members participating in the funeral procession arrived at the designated locations in the four alleys of Gongyuan Road and Changfu Street at the First Park before 4:00 AM. They marched to a point outside Zhongshan Gate, where they formed two lines facing each other. As the coffin passed, the military police stood at attention and saluted, while others removed their hats as a sign of respect. Central Executive and Supervisory Committee members, the Chairman of the National Government, heads of various Yuan and departments, members of the State Funeral Committee, representatives from provincial and municipal party, government, and military organizations, foreign guests, and family members walked to a point outside Zhongshan Gate, where they boarded cars to the cemetery to attend the state funeral. The order of the procession was as follows: First row: One cavalry officer (riding a black horse and carrying the flag to lead the way), two cavalrymen (riding black horses and carrying rifles to protect the flag), two cavalrymen (riding black horses and carrying party and national flags), one company of cavalry with a military band (carrying lances). Second row: Infantry with a military band, one battalion of infantry (with rifles pointing downwards). Third row: Naval military band, naval personnel (with rifles pointing downwards). Fourth row: Police military band, police force. Fifth row: Military band, representatives from agricultural, industrial, commercial, educational, and women's organizations, foreign guests, representatives from overseas Chinese communities, representatives from provincial, municipal, party, government, and military agencies, representatives from Nanjing-based party, government, and military agencies, one company of infantry (with rifles pointing downwards). Sixth row: Central Executive and Supervisory Committee members, the Chairman of the National Government, heads of various Yuan and departments (or their representatives), foreign representatives, members of the State Funeral Committee, relatives and family members. Seventh row: The coffin, family vehicles, one company of infantry (with rifles pointing downwards). Eighth row: One company of cavalry (carrying lances) bringing up the rear. The commander-in-chief of the capital garrison, Gu Zhenglun, served as the overall commander of the procession. Each row had one inspector to direct the Boy Scouts in maintaining order. The Air Force also dispatched two "Caosai" aircraft from the Sixth Squadron to fly alongside the procession.

▲ Foreign Guests: Among the foreign guests were Counselor Fischer of the German Embassy, Counselor Jalle of the Belgian Embassy, Counselor Peck of the United States, the Army Attaché and Naval Attaché of the United States, Consul General Morse of the United Kingdom, Counselor Kenjiro Hayashiide and Counselor/Consul Nakaichi Kamimura of Japan, Naval Captain Nubito Suganuma, Army Attaché Lieutenant Colonel Kumakichi Harada, and the French Consul General.

▲ Family Members Attending: Among the family members of President Tan attending the ceremony were his eldest son, Yi, and daughter-in-law, second son, Bi, three daughters, Xiang, Shu, and Run, nephew Zan, niece Rui, and two sons-in-law, Yuan Siyan and Chen Cheng.

▲ Along the Route: The route from the First Park to the cemetery was guarded by military police. The eighth row of the procession assembled on Gongyuan Road, the seventh row in front of the First Park gate, the sixth row and the portrait car on Fucheng Bridge, the fifth row on Changfu Street, the fourth and third rows in the four alleys, and the second and first rows on Zhongshan Road. All rows were completely assembled before 4:00 AM. After the coffin was moved, each row advanced in order. Central government officials and foreign guests walked with the procession to Zhongshan Gate, where they boarded cars to the cemetery. Chairman Chiang also arrived at Xiaguan at 6:00 AM, where he boarded a car and proceeded to Huangpu Road to join the procession on foot. He personally presided over the funeral rites at the funeral hall.

▲ Cemetery Layout: From the entrance of Linggu Temple to the Lu Tomb, both sides of the road were lined with black and white cloth barriers, interspersed with circular wooden signs bearing the words "State Funeral of President Tan." Tan's tombstone, located next to Linggu Temple, was about two Zhang (approximately 6.6 meters) tall and four Chi (approximately 1.3 meters) wide, made of cement. It was inscribed with the red seal of the "Seal of Honor" and below it were the four seal-script characters of "Tomb of State Funeral." Underneath were the inscriptions "Tomb of Tan Yankai, Former Chairman of the National Government and President of the Executive Yuan of the Republic of China, Central Executive Committee Member of the Chinese Kuomintang," followed by "Respectfully Offered by Chiang Kai-shek on the Fourth Day of September in the Twentieth Year of the Republic of China." In front of the tombstone was a pool, converted from the Dragon Pool of Linggu Temple, about one Zhang deep. The pool was surrounded by a cypress leaf fence decorated with blue flowers. About half a Li (approximately 250 meters) north of the tombstone, the terrain gradually rose, with an ornamental archway bearing the horizontal inscription "The Spirit of Hengshan and Xiangjiang." A little further ahead was the construction site for a memorial hall. Before that was an open space where the coffin was transferred from the hearse to the carrying poles. The hearse, the portrait car, and the family cars stopped here. Three minutes further ahead was a square, the location of the tomb. There was a large ornamental archway with the horizontal inscription "State Funeral Ceremony." On both sides of the road were rest areas for guests and foreign visitors, decorated with black and white plain-colored strips and covered with yellow-green straw mats. Two music stands were located on either side. The funeral hall, erected on the tomb site, was further ahead.

▲ Funeral Hall Layout: The funeral hall was entirely constructed of reed mats, decorated with black and white fabric, and adorned with memorial scrolls. The hall was divided into two parts: the front part served as the ceremonial hall and a rest area for Central Committee members and heads of various departments, while the rear part housed the tomb. A portrait of Tan was hung behind the tomb, with wreaths from Chiang Kai-shek, Ma Fuxiang, and Niu Yongjian placed in front of it, as well as silver wreaths presented by American Minister Johnson and American Consul Peck stationed in Nanjing. Slightly forward was the tomb, constructed entirely of cement and steel, about six Chi deep, five Chi wide, and one Zhang long, with one hundred and ten Jin of realgar (one hundred Jin of Suzhou realgar and ten Jin of Ming realgar) placed underneath to absorb moisture. In the front part of the hall, on either side of the central area used for ceremonies, were rows of desks and chairs. There was also a separate rest area for family members on the left.

The photograph of the coffin after the Transfer Ceremony.

The interment ceremony was attended by all those who participated in the transfer ceremony, as well as Chiang Kai-shek, Li Liejun, Zhang Jingjiang, Shao Yuanchong, Jin Handing, Song Meiling, Zhang Mojun, Li Liejun's wife, Wang Zhengting's wife, Fang Juehui, Zhou Yawei, Jiang Zuobin's wife, Fan Guang, Tao Xuan, and others. At 10:00 AM, the vermilion coffin was placed into the golden tomb, and the interment ceremony commenced. Central Committee members, the Chairman of the National Government, heads of various Yuan and departments, and representatives from various provinces and armies gathered solemnly in the funeral hall. Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government, presided over the ceremony, playing mournful music, offering flowers, reading the eulogy, and delivering the interment declaration, which stated: "On this fourth day of September in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government, the heads of the five Yuan, ministers of various departments, and chairmen of various committees, announce to the coffin of the late President Tan Yankai: We have selected this auspicious day to respectfully hold the state funeral and lay you to rest in this sacred place, to ensure your eternal peace. We offer incense and flowers and humbly present this farewell. May your contributions as a pillar of the nation be forever remembered under the blue sky and white sun, and may the land of dragons and tigers forever protect your resting place." After the moment of silence, the three bows were performed, the mournful music was played, and the sons offered a reply in thanks, and the ceremony was complete. Foreign guests then offered their condolences, followed by officials from various agencies and units, and finally, the family members paid their respects. After the ceremony, personnel from various agencies departed in an orderly manner.

▲ Key Memorial Scrolls: Memorial scrolls sent by various agencies, organizations, and important figures were displayed throughout the funeral hall and the rest areas on both sides. Here are some notable examples: (1) National Government: "You were highly respected in the government, your contributions were great to the party and nation, your name will be remembered throughout the universe, and your spirit will become a star." (2) Chairman Chiang: "You supported the falling and rescued the endangered, with a loyal heart for the party and nation. You worried about the times and grieved for the world, and millions of comrades mourn your passing." (3) Zhang Xueliang: "You were a founding hero, a rare genius in five hundred years. Your military and literary achievements were brilliant. We commend your loyalty and celebrate your glory. Across three thousand Li of distant journey, we send flowers and wine to express our sorrow." (4) Li Liejun: "The sun and moon hang suspended, ghosts and spirits weep in mourning, mountains and forests are forever closed, the court and the people are filled with grief." (5) Wu Peifu: "The roads of Sichuan are difficult, the apes of the Wuxia gorges cry tears in lines. In Changsha, we weep in pain, and the geese returning to Hengyang carry many letters." The upper inscription reads "To Brother An, President [Tan]," and the lower inscription reads "Your younger brother, Wu Peifu." (6) Yu Youren: "Embracing the two sentences of Marquis Wu, you were a complete man of the Republic of China." (7) Dai Chuanxian: "Mount Heng is majestic, towering above all mountains. The autumn wind is desolate, and a great star has fallen." (8) Hu Hanmin: "Auspicious clouds and a bright moon return to heaven, and a gentle spring breeze remains in our hearts."

Work Report from the National Government Disaster Relief Committee in Hankow 64

Committee Member Li Inspects the Jiji Power Plant

Hongshan Shelters 170,000 Flood Victims

The floodwaters in Hankow have gradually receded, bringing some relief to the people. After Chairman Chiang's visit to offer condolences the other day, the Central Government specially dispatched Committee Member Li Jin to Hankow to take charge of disaster relief. Upon arriving in Hankow, Li immediately began planning the relief efforts in detail. The first step was to relocate 170,000 flood victims from the three towns of Wuhan to the vicinity of Hongshan in Wuchang and within Wuhan University, divided into several districts. Each district was assigned medical staff and police officers to prevent epidemics and maintain order. Li visits each district daily to conduct inspections. When a fire broke out at a Texaco facility a few days ago, Li personally boarded a small boat to assist in the rescue, saving hundreds of refugees. The second phase of the plan includes: (1) Establishing a temporary hospital on a large vessel that will travel to the three towns daily to provide medical treatment. Patients can also be admitted to the hospital. Funding has already been secured, and Dr. Wang Zuxiang of the Health Group has been entrusted with planning the details. (2) Renting forty large barges to serve as shelters for the flood victims, divided into five groups. In each group, five barges will serve as shelters, one will serve as an administration office, one as a cooking area, and one as a toilet. This will facilitate relief efforts and prevent the spread of epidemics. (3) Utilizing large pumps to divide the entire city into several districts and pump out the water on a district-by-district basis. During the pumping process, each district will be surrounded by sandbags to prevent the water from flowing back in after it has been pumped out. It is reported that Li greatly admires the Jiji Water and Electricity Plant in the city for its exceptional flood protection measures. Despite the floodwaters being several feet deep throughout the city, the Jiji plant continued to provide water and electricity, making a significant contribution. Therefore, he specially visited the plant yesterday with Advisor Dai and others to inspect the facilities and express his appreciation. He also plans to emulate this effort and utilize the flood victims to pump out the water within a specified timeframe. (4) Erecting wooden planks on the roads to facilitate traffic. This task has been entrusted to the Hubei Branch for speedy implementation.

Situation at the Breach on the East Bank of the Guazhou Yangtze River 65

A dispatch from Zhenjiang reports that since the collapse of more than ten Zhang (approximately 33 meters) of the Guazhou East Yangtze River bank at Majiagang on August 25th, efforts have been underway to rush construction and implement rescue measures in an attempt to repair the breach. However, after a five-day delay, no progress has been made. Currently, the floodwaters have inundated the interior of the enclosure, reaching depths of over one Zhang in low-lying areas and six to seven Chi (approximately 2 to 2.3 meters) in higher areas. People and livestock are being swept away, and homes are being submerged. The situation is extremely tragic. The scope of the disaster area extends east to the Yangzhen motor road (from Shijiaqiao to the riverside), south to the South River bank, west to the East Grand Canal embankment, and north to the inner embankment from Yangzi Bridge to Shijiaqiao. It covers a distance of fifteen Li (approximately 7.5 kilometers) from north to south and eight Li (approximately 4 kilometers) from east to west, totaling an area of one hundred and twenty square Li (approximately 60 square kilometers). Over ten thousand households, a population of sixty to seventy thousand, and over sixty thousand Mu (approximately 40 square kilometers) of farmland have been affected. The extent of the disaster and the severity of the situation are comparable to those of Gaoyou and Shaobo, except that there has fortunately not been any drowning. The flood victims in the area are exposed to the elements, hungry and cold, and mostly gathered on the embankments described above, desperately awaiting relief from the government. (3rd)

Xu Bu Flooded Again 66

Breach in the Dyke at Checun Kou in the North of the City

Wang Jun Issues a Notice to Protect the Old Dyke

A quick dispatch from Xuzhou: Xu Bu experienced continuous heavy rains in early August, causing a breach in the old course of the Yellow River and resulting in flooding. Relief efforts have been underway since then but have yet to reach everyone. Unexpectedly, on the evening of September 1st, the weather changed suddenly, and heavy rain fell again, not stopping until the morning of the 2nd. The relentless downpour caused various parts of the city to become submerged again. Places outside the city, such as the public sports field and the Martyr's Shrine in the city park, were all in the middle of the water. Countless civilian houses were flooded throughout the city. Only Zhongshan and Datong Streets remained unaffected by the water. Collapsed houses and crumbling structures were frequently reported. Those damaged by the previous heavy rain, which were undergoing repairs during the sunny days, collapsed again. The water in the old course of the Yellow River at the northeast and east gates, which had already receded several feet, overflowed the banks again, and houses along the river were submerged. According to the Construction Bureau's measurements, the rainfall in that one night was 150.5 millimeters, equivalent to 4 feet 9.7 inches in the English measurement system. The Flood Relief Committee dispatched personnel to inspect the city and telegraphed the Construction Bureau to dredge the waterways, bringing temporary safety to the city. However, the water from the Weishan Lake north of Xuzhou had already overflowed from Hunan days ago, inundating a vast area of 400 square li. Now, it continues to flow south, passing Wanzhai, located twelve li north of the city. The dyke at Checun Kou, about two li south of Wanzhai, was already in disrepair. On the morning of the 2nd, it suddenly breached amidst wind and rain. Local residents, upon discovering this, immediately gathered to reinforce the breach while reporting to the city. The Construction Bureau dispatched personnel at noon to supervise the emergency repairs, averting a major disaster. The water diverted east from Wanzhai, creating a raging torrent that entered the Jing River. Fortunately, this diversion largely protected the Checun dyke; otherwise, the area north of Bazijie would have been unimaginable. The weather cleared up on the 3rd, and there was generally no danger. However, after the second flooding, relief efforts became even more urgent. Police Commander Wang Jun, based on petitions from citizens, issued a notice to protect the old course of the Yellow River dyke to prevent flooding. The wording was extremely stern, as follows: (According to a report from Liu Zhongxin, the first district chief of Tongshan County, forwarded from citizens Wang Xiyuan, Song Mengjiu, and others, regarding the surge in river water and a proposed construction project to repair the old Yellow River dyke outside the city, requesting a prohibition against military personnel dismantling bricks and stones to prevent river disasters, etc. Based on this, it is found that the area outside Xuzhou City along the old course of the Yellow River is shaped like a cauldron. Every time the river floods, it relies entirely on the surrounding dyke to protect it, preventing the people from being submerged. All the soil, wood, bricks, and stones of the dyke are vitally important to the lives and property of the people of Xuzhou. All local residents and stationed troops should bear full responsibility for its protection. As this command is stationed here, we share the same fate. In addition to ordering the subordinate stationed troops to strictly protect and prohibit dismantling, this notice is hereby issued, urging all military and civilian personnel to be aware. Anyone who dares to dismantle even a single brick or stone of the dyke will be severely punished without leniency upon investigation or denunciation.)

Fujian Flood Victims Desperately Need Relief 67

A dispatch from Fuzhou: Due to the extraordinarily severe disaster situation in the province, the provincial government telegraphed the central government on the 27th and 28th, requesting an allocation of funds for relief. Xu Shiying, chairman of the Central Relief Committee, has already responded with a telegram. The Fujian Provincial Relief Committee also submitted a report to the provincial government, requesting that personnel be sent to various areas for inspection and publicly recommending Provincial Committee member Lin Jinan to go to Beijing to report and request a swift allocation of funds for relief. The telegram report is recorded below:

▲ Xu Shiying's Reply Telegram to Chairman Yang Youjing of the Provincial Government: Brother Youjing, greetings. Your respectful telegram has been received. Fujian Province has suffered from floods and windstorms in recent months, with over ten counties including Liancheng and Yongchun reporting and requesting relief. Reading this, my heart is filled with deep sympathy and admiration. This year's floods are exceptionally severe, and the government has established a Flood Relief Committee to provide assistance. To ensure unified authority, this committee has already submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to transfer all flood relief matters to the Flood Relief Committee for handling. I have noted the information in your telegram and forwarded it to the National Government Flood Relief Committee for review. Respectfully replying, Xu Shiying of the Relief Committee, 28th.

▲ Fujian Relief Committee's Report: Reporting on the matter, since the beginning of summer, the province has experienced continuous rain, causing mountain floods. Areas along rivers and low-lying areas have become submerged. On August 10th, a hurricane suddenly arose, followed by torrential rain, causing widespread devastation and darkness. Disasters occurred frequently, with wind, rain, and floods coming in rapid succession. The damage to houses, crops, fruit trees, human lives, and livestock is incalculable. The affected areas initially included Liancheng, Ningyang, Yong'an, and Minhou, followed by Xiapu, Fuding, Ningde, Gutian, Lianjiang, Luoyuan, Longxi, Puzhao, Anxi, and Yunxiao counties. The number of unreported counties is unknown. Although the disaster situation is not as severe as in Jiangsu and Hubei, the people are already suffering deeply. At the tenth meeting of this committee on August 31st of this year, it was decided that the wind, rain, and flood disasters in various counties were extensive and severe. In addition to ordering the counties of Yong'an, Gutian, and Lianjiang to conduct separate investigations, personnel should be dispatched to the Fuding-Ningde area and the Zhangzhou area to investigate the disaster situation, take photos, and report via telegram. First, report to the central government and the Executive Yuan, requesting a large allocation of funds for relief. Furthermore, Committee Member Lin Jinan was recommended to report to Nanjing, requesting a swift allocation of funds, etc. In addition to handling these matters separately, we respectfully submit this report to the government for review. Respectfully presented to Yang, Chairman of the Fujian Provincial Government (September 1st).

Central Committee's General Report on the Wuhu Disaster Situation 68

204,000 Refugees

4,000 Unburied Dead

Ordinary Water Depth Exceeds Ten Feet

A dispatch from Wuhu: The flood disaster in Anhui Province is widespread and severe. The central government dispatched special commissioners Zhuang Yan and others to Anhui, dividing them into five groups for investigation. The southern and central Anhui counties were assigned to Central Committee member Qian Danwu and Wen Yi of the Provincial Department of Construction. Qian and others arrived in Wuhu and, together with representatives from the Wuhu, Fan, and Wu counties' Relief Association, chartered a special boat yesterday morning to depart from Wuhu and inspect the disaster areas of Fenglin, Xingchun, Wanchun, Sanshui, Pujia Dian, and Qingshui River. Along the way, everything was submerged in water, making it difficult to distinguish between fields and dikes, making navigation extremely difficult. Since the storm, about 4,000 refugees have been swept into the water and drowned. Floating corpses were everywhere. Countless pigs and cattle created an overwhelming stench that made people nauseous. Those trapped in the water without any means of escape used ropes and wooden objects to tie themselves to trees in an attempt to find refuge and await rescue. Qian and others, upon seeing such a tragic scene, rushed back to Wuhu that evening to telegraph the central government and the Anhui Provincial Government, reporting the actual situation of the disaster areas. They requested that Wuhu be classified as a first-class disaster area and that a large sum of money be quickly allocated for immediate relief to save the dying refugees. The general report on the disaster situation is as follows: (1) The disaster area in this county covers 2,560 square kilometers. (2) The current number of refugees is over 204,500. (3) 89,600 people have been displaced by the disaster. (4) The number of refugee deaths exceeds 4,000. (5) Property losses amount to 14 million yuan. (6) Over 498,700 mu of farmland have been flooded. (7) Crop failure is expected to result in 50,000 refugees. (8) The ordinary water depth exceeds ten feet, making it impossible to replant other crops. (9) The most urgent need now is to distribute immediate relief. (10) Since the flood, the price of rice has risen from eight yuan to thirteen yuan. After completing their work in Wuhu, the commissioners boarded a boat this morning to proceed to Fanchang (2nd).

Military Bandits Cause Havoc in Shanxi Province 69

Mutiny of Troops Stationed Outside Taiyuan City

Bandit Forces in Various Counties Divided into Four Groups

A dispatch from Taiyuan: Banditry in Shanxi Province has become increasingly rampant recently. Urgent telegrams have been pouring in from various districts, indicating an unmanageable situation. At the same time, incidents of troop mutiny are still being reported. Recently, a mutiny occurred among the troops stationed at the Civil Aviation Bureau (i.e., the aviation airfield, located over twenty li outside the North Gate of Taiyuan). The combination of military and banditry has created a dire situation in Shanxi. The recent banditry situation is recorded as follows:

▲ Mutiny of Troops in Taiyuan At 1:30 AM on August 29th, a platoon leader named Zhang of the 6th Company, 2nd Battalion, 2nd Regiment of the garrison troops protecting the aircraft at the Civil Aviation Bureau outside the North Gate, suddenly led forty to fifty soldiers in a mutiny. At the beginning of the incident, they launched a surprise attack on the company commander, Guo, shooting him. Although the shot was not fatal, it caused severe injuries. A guard named Han was shot and killed. They also cut the telephone lines to prevent news from leaking. When the mutinous soldiers were shooting the company commander, Chen, another platoon leader, seeing the situation was bad, quickly ordered his platoon soldiers to prepare live ammunition. By dawn, they had found the company commander and carried him to the hospital for treatment. Upon hearing the news, the regiment immediately dispatched a battalion of troops, guided by two soldiers who had escaped, to pursue and suppress the mutineers in the direction of Xialan Village and Yangdian. The cause of the mutiny was said to be that the bureau was scheduled to pay wages on that day, and the soldiers became greedy and initiated the riot.

▲ Bandits of Xi County Besiege the City According to provincial government sources, there have been many reports of banditry from counties in northern and southern Shanxi in recent days. Yesterday, a telegram from Xi County reported that bandits in the county were rampant and attempting to besiege the county seat. Many wealthy families have been kidnapped for ransom, and communist bandits have infiltrated the bandit groups, distributing leaflets. Yang Yaofang has dispatched troops to pursue and suppress them overnight. Given the bandit activity in various locations, three areas have been designated, with each general responsible for suppression. However, a dedicated person is also needed to manage the overall plan. Provincial Government Chairman Chou Dai intends to telegraph Chairman Xu to return to Taiyuan as soon as possible after completing his affairs in Beiping to handle the bandit suppression in various counties. In addition, disaster relief will be provided to areas severely affected by banditry.

▲ Recent Situation of Military Suppression of Bandits Banditry has been rampant in various counties recently. Nine out of ten counties in southern and northern Shanxi are plagued by bandits. Artillery Supervisor Zhou Dai recently gave a talk on the recent situation of bandit suppression, stating that the bandit areas in the province can be roughly divided into four locations: (1) The Guangling-Hunyuan area, (2) the Tianzhen area, (3) the Xingxian-Linxian-Lanxian area, (4) the Puxian-Xixian area. First, the bandits in the Guangling-Hunyuan area are the mutinous soldiers of Gao Guizi's troops. Initially, there were over 300 people, who arrived at Xiaguan via Jiehuang Ridge. Commander Li Fuying was telegraphed to suppress them overnight. They then fled into Donghe and Zhen, and regrouped to Hunyuan via Gushu and Zhao Bi, with 500 to 600 people. They then fled into Yingxian Dasuinian Village, about 700 to 800 strong, gaining even greater momentum. Passing through Daiyue and other places, they reached the vicinity of Pinglu, where they gathered over a thousand more defeated soldiers. They looted Xiaoshikou in Shanyin and fled into Youyu County. This group of bandits, under the command of Commander Zhao Chengzhou, was fiercely suppressed by two cavalry regiments, an artillery company, and a battalion of infantry under Zhang Huizhao. They have never stopped, and have now left the province. Secondly, the bandits in the Tianzhen area are the notorious bandit Wang Damei, originally from Shi Yousan's troops. After their defeat, they fled to the south bank of the Sanggan River and to places such as Futugou and Panjiashan in that county, totaling several hundred people. They then fled south into Guangling County and north into Tianzhen Wujiashan. Commander Zhao Chengzhou and Commander Zhang Huizhao ordered the troops under their command to jointly suppress this group. According to recent telegrams from Zhao Chengzhou and Zhang Huizhao, the remnants of Gao's mutinous soldiers have fled to Qingshuihe in Suiyuan Province via Qidunkou, and the defeated soldiers of Shi have fled into Xinghe. It can be said that the two groups of bandits in northern Shanxi have been completely eliminated as of today. The bandits in the Xingxian-Linxian-Lanxian area are the bandits of Shaanxi origin, Ji Laoliu and others, who fled from Dadu Mountain to the Dawan Mountain and Bailong Mountain areas via Xingxian. They then fled to Dongcunzhen in Lanxian, then to Jingle and Loufanzhen. They then fled to Jierwu in Kelan and were suppressed by the county's defense forces, fleeing to Xintunbao in Ningwu. There were also over 300 bandits who fled into Lanxian from Fangshan. Dozens of mounted bandits were also located in Wanjagou. Over 300 bandits were located in the Northwest Sea area. The first battalion of the Third Security Regiment arrived and dispersed and eliminated these bandits. In addition, over 300 bandits gathered in Linxian, and over 100 bandits gathered in Hejiawan in Xingxian. Commander Yang Yaofang of Dagu and Regimental Commander Zhao of Fenyang ordered their subordinates to suppress them vigorously. Other counties, such as Xiaoyi, Zhongyang, and Wuzhai, have also experienced minor disturbances from small groups of bandits, which should not be difficult to eliminate. The bandits in the Puxian-Xixian area include six to seven hundred bandits in Laoye Ridge in Puxian and Kangchengzhen in Xi County. A total of over 2,000 bandits are in the connected mountains of Zhongyang, Shilou, Yonghe, Pu, and Xi counties. In addition, bandits from Anze fled to Shilicun in Qin County, and over 200 bandits from Fenxi plundered wantonly before fleeing to the Gongjiadian Mountains on the border of Pu, Zhao, and Fen counties. Recently, their ranks have been swelling, and Commander Yang Chengyuan and Commander Yang Yaofang have been jointly tasked with suppressing them (August 30th).

President of the South Manchurian Railway Company Talks in Harbin 70

The South Manchurian Railway Company's Policy of Austerity Has Been Completed

Leaving Harbin to Go to Liaoning and then Inspect Andong

A dispatch from Harbin: President Uchida Kosai and Vice President Eguchi Sadame of the South Manchurian Railway Company, along with seventeen staff members, passed through the Ha-Man line from the Tao-Ang Road to Harbin on the evening of August 29th. The East China Railway Company dispatched staff in advance to take a special train to Ang'angxi Station to greet them. The special train arrived at the station at 9 PM on the 29th. Over 300 people, including heads of various Harbin agencies and important Japanese and Russian figures, welcomed them at the station. The station was crowded with people inside and out. The Special District Police Department and the Railway Police Department both sent large detachments of armed police to protect the station. After Uchida and his party got off the train, they met with the welcoming guests in the VIP waiting room and then went to the South Manchurian Railway Company's Harbin Office in Qinjia Gang to stay. The accompanying staff members, including Director Shoto, Kimura, Military Advisor Hayashi, Director Shanxi, Secretary Yagi, Secretary Sugiki, Section Chief Nakamura, and Section Chief Matsukura, all stayed at the North Manchuria Hotel. On the morning of the 30th, they visited the official residence of our Special District. In the evening, they attended a banquet hosted by the Japanese Residents Association. On the 31st, they visited the city streets and industries. In the evening, they attended a banquet hosted by Russian officials of the East China Railway Company. They are scheduled to leave Harbin for Changchun at 8:50 AM on the 1st. On the afternoon of the 30th, several Chinese and foreign reporters visited. According to President Uchida, "I went to Russia from Vladivostok once before and passed through Harbin. This is my second time here. However, this is the first time I have traveled by train on a Chinese state-owned railway (i.e., the Qiqihar-Taonan Railway). When I arrived in Qiqihar, I visited the Chinese city and was very satisfied. I will travel from Harbin to Changchun, then to Jilin, and return to Liaoning via the Ji-Hai Railway. I will transfer to the Bei-Ning Railway to Yingkou, and then return to Liaoning and Ning via Yingkou, transferring to the An-Feng train to Andong. I can visit all the railways in the Northeast on this itinerary. Manchuria is vast and rich in resources. The South Manchurian, East China, and Wuli Railways can all cooperate in the spirit of mutual benefit. There are many ports of export for the various railways in the three eastern provinces, such as Vladivostok, Dalian, Andong, Yingkou, and Huludao. These ports have a very important relationship to the development of the region. The South Manchurian Railway Company hopes that the Chinese railways can develop with the assistance of these ports. The South Manchurian Railway Company's layoffs have now been completed and cannot be reduced further. The details of the South Manchurian Railway Company's subsidiary business have not yet been finalized. As for the joint operation of the East, Wuli, and South Manchurian Railways, I do not know of any plans to convene a meeting in Harbin, as I left Dalian very early." (30th)

Zhu Mao and Other Bandits Suddenly Flee South 71

Gong, Han, and Jiang Divisions Separately Block and Suppress

A dispatch from Nanchang: Zhu Mao, Peng, Huang, and other bandits recently gathered their remnants and concentrated them in the mountains near Liangcun, Longgang, Huangpi, Xiaopu, Donggu in Ningdu, Yudu, Yongfeng, and Xingguo, and in the vicinity of Gu Longgang. They launched a large-scale counterattack. After fierce suppression by the local garrison troops in battles such as Dajinzhu, Longgang, Datian, Junbu, and others, several thousand bandits were killed. Zhu Mao and others, knowing they could not succeed, changed their plans and attempted to flee to the Guangdong border. Upon receiving the report, the Command ordered the 19th Route Army to follow and pursue them, ordering the Gong, Luo, and Han divisions to set up guard on the east bank of the Wan-Tai-Gan River. They also ordered Squadron Leader Tian of the air force to lead five Douglas fighter planes to the Xingguo area to coordinate with the right-wing army and eliminate the bandits. Squadron Leader Tian telegraphed from Ji'an on the afternoon of the 28th, saying that he had taken heavy bombs and machine guns and flown to the Liantang area for reconnaissance and bombing. About five li east of Liantang, they saw three to four thousand remaining bandits in an open area, their ranks disorganized and their heads huddled together, seemingly holding a meeting. Upon seeing the plane, they were about to scatter and flee. The plane dropped over thirty heavy bombs and strafed with machine guns. The bandits fell one after another. There were probably less than a thousand survivors.

Because Zhu Mao planned to flee south, they ordered Huang Gonglue's pseudo-Third Army and the Xingtai pseudo-police force to commandeer dozens of civilian boats in Xikou and Hongfu and cross the river first. Gong Bingfan and Han Deqin's divisions, upon hearing the news, immediately moved horizontally between Xingguo and Taihe and sandwiched them on the opposite bank. Bandit corpses clogged the river. Han telegraphed the province yesterday to report the victory, briefly stating that over two thousand remaining bandits in the Xikou and Hongfu area commandeered boats on the morning of the 27th, attempting to cross the river and flee south. He then notified the Gong division and troops, who intercepted them at Fenghuanggang. He personally led Zhang's brigade and a regiment of Wang's brigade to ambush the bandits from behind. As the bandits were crossing the river, his troops and the Gong division's troops arrived and attacked them from across the river. The bandits in the middle of the river and on the river beaches had no cover. After five hours of fierce shooting, bandit corpses clogged the river, turning the water red. Eighteen boats were sunk. The bandits were completely annihilated in this battle. According to wounded bandits, they intended to flee to the San-Nan area. An inspection of the bandit corpses revealed that they were from the pseudo-Third Army and the Xingtai County Red Guard Police Battalion. Over 400 guns, spears, and broadswords were seized (August 30th).

Han Fuqu and Jiang Bocheng Return to Jinan 72

Peng Shibin, Representative of Zhang Xueliang Stationed in Jinan, Accompanies Them

A dispatch from Jinan: Provincial Government Chairman Han Fuqu and Jiang Bocheng went to Beiping a few days ago to discuss the security of North China and the issue of Yan and Feng going abroad with Deputy Commander Zhang. They left Beiping with their staff and guards at 9:20 AM yesterday (2nd) and arrived in Dezhou at 6:30 PM. After getting off the train, they summoned Zhao Xin's Third Regiment of the 59th Brigade of the 20th Division and Xie Shujie's troops of the 20th Division for a talk. At 7:15 PM, they left Dezhou by train and arrived in Jinan at 10:50 PM. Those who welcomed them at the station included the provincial party headquarters, the provincial government, Chief of Staff Li Zongbi of the General Command, Sun Tongxuan of the 20th Division, Cao Fulin of the 29th Division, and Gu Liangmin of the 22nd Division. Security was tightened along the route from the station to the provincial government. There were also security teams on the platform. After Han, Jiang, and others got off the train and shook hands with the welcoming crowd, they met with reporters. According to Jiang Bocheng, the results of this trip were extremely satisfactory. After this unity, the generals of North China all unanimously followed the Commander-in-Chief and Deputy Commander-in-Chief and supported the central government. Yan Xishan must go abroad. Chairman Xu (Yongchang) has sent a representative to Shanxi to persuade him. The Deputy Commander-in-Chief and Chairman Han have also sent representatives to urge him to leave. The situation in North China is very optimistic. Han Fuqu also said that the results of this trip were very good. The generals of the provinces north of the Yangtze River all went to Beiping this time. Deputy Commander Zhang was very frank, and the generals were very moved. There will definitely be no problems north of the Yangtze River in the future. Mr. Yan must go abroad. Chairman Xu (Yongchang) has sent a representative to persuade Yan. This is the first step. There are also second and third steps that have been determined but have not yet been announced. The military and government officials of the Northeast Army are not arrogant and are approachable, which is especially pleasing. He will go to Henan in three to five days to discuss the matters of cleaning up the rural areas of Shandong and Henan with Chairman Liu. Those who came with them also included Ge Guangting, Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, and Peng Shibin, Counselor of the Northeast Border Defense Military Commander-in-Chief's Office, representative of Deputy Commander Zhang. Peng said that he had no special mission in coming here, but was ordered by the Deputy Commander to be stationed in Jinan to contact Chairman Han in case of an emergency (September 2nd).

Bandit Strength in Eastern Hubei Has Declined 73

Xu Yuanquan Personally Goes to the Front to Supervise Suppression

Bandits Flee into the Mountains Between Huangmei and Guangji

A dispatch from Hankou: The various counties in eastern Hubei have been quite stable since the communist bandits were suppressed. Unexpectedly, several thousand communist bandits from Yingshan in Anhui Province suddenly invaded during this flood disaster, calling themselves the pseudo-Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army. They were very rampant. The county seats of Qishui and Guangji fell one after another, and they besieged the county seat of Huangmei for two days. County Magistrate Gui Fucang of the county led the militia to resist with all their might, and fortunately they were preserved. After receiving the report, He Chengjunn, Director of the Wuhan Garrison Command, immediately dispatched Supervisor Xu Yuanquan to personally supervise the suppression. Xu left on August 30th, leading Xu Jiwu's brigade and Zhang Zhenhan's division and Ding's brigade, heading straight to Qishui. At the same time, the troops stationed in Susong in Anhui Province and the troops stationed in Jiujiang in Jiangxi Province also set out separately to launch a large-scale encirclement and suppression. Knowing they could not resist, the bandits abandoned Qishui and retreated to the mountains between Huangmei and Guangji, hoping to flee back to their old base in Yingshan. The people of Huangmei and Guangji have suffered both from the flood disaster and the bandit disaster, and they are all in extreme pain. It is said that they have sent representatives to Hankou to petition the Garrison Command, hoping that the suppression troops will quickly eliminate the remaining bandits to prevent future troubles, and have telegraphed the Yongsu military ship to petition Commander-in-Chief Chiang (September 1st).

Case of Yichang County Magistrate Zhao Tiegong Flogging a County Resident to Death 74

The County Party Committee Petitions the Control Yuan to Impeach

Yichang Dispatch: Since Zhao Tiegong became the magistrate of Yichang County, accusations against him have piled up like a forest. However, due to the protection of powerful figures, the people of Yichang could do nothing about it. On July 4th, Zhao's concubine, dressed in strange attire, paraded through the market, attracting a crowd of onlookers. Three local residents, Yang Shanmei, Yang Bangmo, and Qu Linyun, also followed behind, whispering among themselves. This was overheard by Zhao's guards, who immediately arrested the three men. Zhao ordered the constables to inflict severe beatings, personally wielding the rod to flog each of them dozens of times. The three men, exhausted and speechless, were on the verge of death before being imprisoned in the main jail. The next day, Yang Shanmei died in prison from severe injuries. Lu Guojun, the Yichang prison warden, reported the matter to the Yichang District Court. The court dispatched Chief Prosecutor Wang Yanshen and Coroner Li Lianqing to conduct an autopsy. The autopsy revealed that Yang Shanmei's legs, arms, and knees were all red, swollen, and lacerated, confirming that he died from injuries. Simultaneously, it was also verified that Yang Bangmo and Qu Linyun had injuries on their arms. Prosecutor Wang immediately filled out an autopsy report, along with injury reports and oral statements, which were attached to the case file. Subsequently, Chief Prosecutor Chen Shi sent a letter to Zhao Tiegong, summoning him to court for questioning. After receiving the letter, Zhao had no choice but to reply to the court, claiming that Yang Shanmei, who died in custody due to injuries, was captured by Liu Zhongyi, the acting captain of the militia, during a patrol because the three men were allegedly engaged in robbery. Prosecutor Chen found this account to be implausible as there was no specific information about the location or victim of the alleged robbery. He sent a reply requesting that Liu Zhongyi be brought to court for questioning. At this point, Zhao realized he had made a blunder and consulted with Liu Zhongyi. Liu firmly denied the allegations. Later, a soldier named Lai Zhaoyan was presented as Liu to appear in court. During the prosecutor's interrogation, Lai Zhaoyan was told that the murderer must pay with his life. Lai Zhaoyan was terrified and confessed that he was impersonating Liu and that he was instructed to do so by Director Zhao of the airfield. Based on this testimony, the prosecutor sent another letter to Director Zhao. The county government replied, stating that no one by the name of Zhao Jingqing was currently employed, and that that person had been dismissed from his post for a long time. As a result, the court found the matter increasingly difficult to handle. Yuan Yong, a member of the Yichang County Party Committee, filed a complaint with the provincial government, accusing Zhao Tiegong of perverting the law. After receiving the complaint, Provincial Chairman He Chengjun telegraphed Yuan Bin, Chief of Staff to Liu Xiang, stationed in Yichang, inquiring whether Zhao Tiegong had indeed committed illegal acts of murder. Yuan replied by telegram, confirming the facts. Chairman He then telegraphed the Yichang Court, ordering that the case files of the Yang case be quickly transferred to the military headquarters for review. Chief Prosecutor Chen Shi immediately replied by telegram, stating that the case files of the Yang case had already been transferred to the Prosecutor's Office of the High Court. Therefore, the files were not sent to the provincial government. However, Yuan Yong, a member of the Party Committee, believed that the case had already been filed with the provincial government but had not yet yielded results. He then filed a complaint with the National Government's Control Yuan. The petition read as follows: (The case involves Zhao Tiegong's concubine. On July 4th, dressed in male Western attire, she drove through the city, passing through Gulou Street. Yang Shanmei, a shop assistant at Yifeng Store, Yang Bangmo, an apprentice tailor at Wu Youtai Tailor Shop, and Qu Linyun, found it strange and speculated whether she was a man or a woman. This was overheard by the accompanying guards, who arrested the shop assistant and apprentice and brought them to the county government where they were brutally beaten and imprisoned in the main jail. On the next day (July 5th), Yang Shanmei died in prison due to severe injuries. Yang Bangmo and Qu Linyun were also severely beaten and were on the verge of death. These facts have been reported to the Control Yuan and have been separately investigated and verified by the Yichang District Court Prosecutor's Office. However, the county magistrate has refused to appear in court, making it impossible to exercise judicial power. The Prosecutor's Office has gathered all the case files and evidence and transferred them to the Hubei High Court Prosecutor's Office for legal proceedings. Currently, during the period of political tutelage and after the promulgation of the Provisional Constitution, the county magistrate, as the head of the county government, should strictly abide by laws and regulations and protect human rights. However, he abused his authority over a minor incident involving his concubine's strange appearance, disregarding human life and violating the Provisional Constitution to the extreme. The deceased's family, shop owner, and the entire population of Yichang are filled with uncontrollable indignation at Zhao Tiegong's illegal killing, but they dare not speak out due to his oppressive power. The county magistrate, aware that his crime is unforgivable, has fled to the provincial capital under the pretext of resigning. The entire population of Yichang resents Zhao Tiegong for evading justice. It is said that the Hubei Provincial Government intends to reinstate him, which is perplexing. At a time when legal rights are being negotiated, foreigners often use the poor state of Chinese law as their excuse. After news of Zhao Tiegong's illegal killing spread, consulates of various countries stationed in Yichang have been paying close attention. Yet the Hubei Provincial Government not only fails to impose severe punishment but intends to reinstate him. What is the intention? This is something that Chinese and foreigners alike cannot comprehend. How can this be called judicial reform or the promulgation of the Provisional Constitution? Is it not giving more excuses to those at home and abroad? As a party member serving in the Yichang Party Committee, Yuan Yong is heartbroken and cannot remain silent in the face of Zhao Tiegong's trampling of human life and disregard for the law. He feels compelled to uphold the Provisional Constitution, value human rights, and speak up for the people. In addition to requesting the Hubei Provincial Party Committee to send another letter to the provincial government to investigate the matter according to law, he submits this document along with a copy of the original case files and injury reports transferred from the Yichang District Court Prosecutor's Office to the Control Yuan for review. He urgently requests that the Control Yuan impeach Zhao Tiegong according to law and order the Hubei Provincial Government to arrest and investigate Zhao Tiegong, who is arrogant, reckless, and inhumane, in order to uphold justice and redress grievances. He awaits orders with utmost urgency. Respectfully submitted to President Yu of the Control Yuan of the National Government, Yuan Yong, Member of the Yichang County Party Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party. (Original case files and injury reports transferred from the Yichang District Court Prosecutor's Office omitted.)

Local Correspondence

Suzhou 75

Higher Court Re-Appoints Prison Wardens in Various Counties: Yesterday (the 4th), the High Court announced the appointment of Cai Zhaohong as the prison warden of Jinshan County. Peng Jicheng, Section Chief of the Second Section of the Third Prison, was transferred to Siyang as prison warden. Jin Changnian, the prison warden of Gaoyou, is awaiting further assignment. Zheng Ruiyun, the prison warden of Taicang, was transferred to succeed him. Liu Jingyi was appointed to succeed as the prison warden of Taicang County. Wu Shutang was also appointed to act as trial judge in Shuyang County.

Prisoners Transferred from Gaoyou and Dongtai: According to a report from the Magistrate of Gaoyou County, due to the flooding, he requested that the prisoners be transferred to other counties. President Lin ordered the county magistrate to transfer forty prisoners to the Jiangning Detention Center and eighty-three prisoners to the Zhenjiang Prison. It is also said that all prisoners from Dongtai County were transferred to the Fourth Prison in Nantong.

Bandit Activity Near Taihu Lake on the Rise Again: Banditry remains rampant in various areas along Taihu Lake in Wujiang. At 3 PM on the 31st of last month, fishermen Chen Jingchun and his wife, Qin, were fishing on the shore of Taihu Lake in Wujiang when a bandit boat suddenly appeared. Two bandits jumped out, pointed guns at the boat, and kidnapped Chen Jingchun and his wife. Yesterday (the 4th), the county government of Wujiang consulted with the County Magistrate of Wu here and ordered the subordinates to assist in the arrest. According to information from the water police, since the search and suppression by the water and land military police brigade, the main gangs of lake bandits have hidden in extremely secret locations and do not appear frequently. They usually dispatch small groups to carry out kidnappings.

Songjiang 76

Local Figures Request Arrest of Remaining Bandits: The bandit leader Lu Yaosheng, a former pseudo-regimental commander under the bandit leader Taibao Ashu, used to make a living selling salt along the coast of Jinshan. After meeting Taibao Ashu last year, he gathered dozens of followers and joined the bandit ranks. He was captured by the Fengxian County police and has been sent to the Songjiang Pacification Sub-district Command for interrogation. However, local figures in Songjiang and Jinshan believe that although the bandit Lu has been arrested, his henchmen are hiding in various towns in Punan, Tinglin, Shanyang, and Zhalin. If a strict arrest is not carried out in a timely manner, it may lead to future troubles. They have compiled a list of the names of the escaped bandits and submitted it to the military and police authorities, requesting a thorough search and arrest.

Jiangyin 77

Villagers Assault Police in Sueshu Bridge Township: Wang Wenzhong, the chief of the Fourth Sub-bureau of the Seventh District Yangshe Public Security Bureau, dispatched patrol leader Ying Guixin with fourteen police officers, armed, to Hongfu Teahouse in Sueshu Bridge to arrest gamblers one afternoon. They arrested seven gamblers on the spot and seized mahjong tiles, playing cards, etc. Three gamblers, Sun Yaoguan, Chen Genyun, and Chen Qingbao, jumped from the upper floor and were injured. Chen Qingbao died from his abdominal injuries at midnight. A group of villagers, including stonemason A'er, gathered and seized the arrested gamblers, snatched firearms from the police officers, and opened fire, wounding police officer Zhang Zhensheng and assaulting Xu Rongrui, Li Sihai, Li Deyu, and cook Wu A'gen. Six bolt-action rifles with twenty-two rounds of ammunition and two box-type pistols with sixty rounds of ammunition were seized. Around 9 PM, the Huashe and Yangshe Militia arrived, but the villagers remained aggressive. District Chief Wang Wenkui's hat and clothes were torn, and militia members were beaten. On the morning of the 2nd, Bureau Chief Wang sent the seriously injured Zhang Zhensheng and Xu Rongrui to the Gospel Hospital for treatment, while Ji Deyu and others went to the county to have their injuries examined. County Magistrate Peng opened a court session and ordered officials to examine and verify the injuries, pending review and handling.

Nantong 78

Relief Ships Continuously Head to Xingdong: More than thirty relief ships for Xinghua and Dongtai were requisitioned from the four villages on the 3rd, towed to Anfeng by small steamers. The second relief team, carrying large quantities of dry food and pickles, set off with the ships.

Efforts to Repair Breaches in River Embankment: The Nantong river embankment was breached by the high tide, causing tidal damage from Yaogang in the west to Xiangshan in the east. Water flooded above the roofs of various enclosures. The water has now receded completely, resulting in significant losses. As the autumn flood season is approaching, the Construction Bureau is supervising the repair of the breaches.

Ministry of Military Affairs Urges Settlement of the Sulang Military Field Case: The Ministry of Military Affairs investigated the military fields of the former Suzhen Langshan two camp and found that they had been seized by the Tonghai Reclamation and Pastoral Company. The National Government approved the matter and ordered the company to pay the price of the land. If they were unwilling to comply, the land would be reclaimed. Minister He ordered the Nantong County Government on the 3rd to promptly handle and report the settlement in accordance with the National Government's order.

Difficulty in Reorganizing the Militia: The Nantong County Government has repeatedly received orders from the province urging the reorganization of the official militia. County Magistrate Huang convened a meeting of all district militia chiefs and resolved that it would be difficult to draw recruits for the reorganization of the militia in the near future. The recruitment system would still be used, and the county government would report to the province for a delay. Militia expenses would be shared by merchants and farmers according to the newly established funding standards. Farmers would pay based on their land acreage, and merchants would pay based on their capital amount to determine the amount of fees to be paid.

Rugao 79

Shen Zhongmo's Coffin Opened for Examination: Shen Zhongmo, who resided in Shuidongkou in the southwest township of Lugang, was dragged to the residence of the local bandit Ji Guo and was hacked to death with a large knife by Ji Guo and his accomplices Shen Yizhai, Sun Shenger, Sun Diancong, and Xu Zhuyu in July of last year. Shen's family reported the matter to the county government, requesting justice. The county government secretly ordered Chen Qingxun, the captain of the Second County Police Squad, to arrest Ji Guo and hand him over to the county for interrogation and sentencing to life imprisonment. However, the bandit refused to accept the verdict and filed an appeal. The High Court ruled that the case of the bandit killing was already proven to be true and ordered the county government to transport the coffin of the victim Shen Zhongmo to the city for examination to verify the truth in order to proceed with the legal process. After receiving the order, the county government dispatched Investigator Guo and Coroner Zhang to the Dajiao Field outside the west gate today (the 2nd) to open the coffin for examination.

Wuxi 80

Chinese and Western Doctor Qin Liujiang Kills a Person: A woman surnamed Zhou, the wife of Zhou Zihui, a resident of Meichekou near Zhangshe in the northern township of this county, had given birth to too many children and was feeling sorry for herself. She then took abnormal measures to induce an abortion, which resulted in chills and fever. Her family hired the Chinese and Western doctor Qin Liujiang to treat her. After examining her, the doctor claimed that her condition was critical and that she needed an emergency injection, but the price of the medicine and injection would be twenty-six yuan and five jiao. The family agreed. Dr. Qin then performed the operation and gave the injection. However, Zhou's wife's condition not only did not improve but worsened after the injection. She died the day before yesterday. Zhou Zihui, grieving over the tragic death of his wife, has filed a complaint with Qin Liujiang. It is not known what the outcome will be.

He'erlukou Robbery Case Solved: Shen, the district chief of the Second District of the Provincial Water Police Team stationed in Xix, received a tip-off that several bandits who robbed the Su Shunji grocery store opened by Su Guoxiang in the He'erlukou area of the Fourth District were hiding in a certain township. District Chief Shen immediately dispatched Inspector Xiong Bin of the district headquarters to lead detectives to the township to arrest them. They captured a bandit named Tang Jinbao in Jingyun City in the southern township, and then captured bandits Wang Maolang and Chen Baolang in a thatched shed on Yangming Road. They were immediately brought back to the district headquarters for questioning. Tang and the other two confessed to robbing the Su family and another family, and admitted that they had only robbed eighty-five yuan in silver dollars from the Su family, sixty-three yuan in silver dollars and clothing from the other family. There were a total of six people involved. Inspector Xiong then reported to District Chief Shen yesterday for review and handling.

Remnants of the Red Spear Society Found in Wangfang Village: Most of the residents of Xiwangfang Village near Yanqiao in the Fifth District of the county are engaged in the business of supporting rice boats and traveling to Shangxingbu in Liyang, etc. They are deeply superstitious about the Red Spear Society. Recently, a group of young boatmen invited three Red Spear Society members from Jintan to the village to serve as instructors. There are already more than fifty people who have joined and are learning. Every night at 9 PM, they burn incense and practice with incantations. District Chief Zhu Chenghong and Fu Qin, the chief of the Thirteenth Public Security Bureau, are sincerely afraid of the spread of heresy. Yesterday, they dispatched police to secretly investigate the truth and immediately disbanded the society.

Changzhou 81

Signs of a Business Partner Absconding: The Yongfengsheng Timber Shop in the western suburbs of Wuyi was previously cheated of nine thousand four hundred yuan by a partner who absconded. After searching everywhere, there was no news. It has now been learned that the absconding person was Xi Zhenxiang, a clerk. He recently sent a letter from Tianjin to Changzhou, stating that he was fooled by his colleague Song Weiqing. He admitted that he had absconded with five thousand four hundred yuan and fled. He would return to Changzhou immediately to return it. The remaining four thousand yuan was taken by Song Weiqing. The day before yesterday, Xi did come to Changzhou from Tianjin and returned four thousand five hundred yuan, claiming that he had already spent several hundred yuan. The timber shop then arrested Song Weiqing and questioned him about the money, but his words were evasive. They immediately filed a lawsuit with the court to recover the money.

Yangzhou 82

Police Detectives Rescue Kidnapped Victim: Li Qingyu, a resident of Lijia Ao in Xianzhen, Yidu County, reported that his four-year-old son, Xiaoxizi, was kidnapped by a gang of bandits in the spring. Detective Sun Xuewen and Gao Baolian from the county government and Detective Wang Longzhang and Zhou Fengqi from the First Public Security Bureau went to Caojiaba in Xiannvzhen on the afternoon of the 2nd and learned about the location of the bandits and the victim. They were refused when they went to arrest them, and a fight ensued for an hour. The bandits fled. They were chased to the Caishi Intersection in Xianzhen, where bandit Li Wenyu was captured and Xiaoxizi, the kidnapped victim, was rescued. At 9 AM on the morning of the 3rd, they were escorted to Yangzhou City and sent to the county government's detective team to be detained for interrogation.

Ningbo 83

Central Committee Member Cai Yuanpei Leaves Ningbo for Beijing: Mr. Cai Yuanpei, a member of the Central Committee, came to Ningbo the day before yesterday at the invitation of Ma Yinchu, the president of the Chinese Economic Society, to give a speech. This morning (the 3rd) he took the early train to Hangzhou and then transferred to Beijing.

Encircling and Suppressing New Bandit Gangs: Xu Mazhan Village in Lianshan District, Fenghua, has repeatedly received threatening letters from bandit leader Mao Pengxing, instructing them to raise six thousand yuan in silver dollars immediately, causing great panic among the people of the village. Village Chief Wang Changyang reported the information to the county. County Magistrate Zhang ordered the County Militia to suppress them. Captain Mao ordered the deputy captains stationed at Yantouxia, Shimen Huxiao Tushao, Wanwan, Dajian, and Jianxia, to encircle and suppress the bandits at Wangshakeng on August 31st. However, there were no traces of bandits, so they all returned to their defense posts. The Ying Family in Jinyun was Robbed: Ying Jinyun, a resident of Dachengjia Road in Dinghai Village, Fifth District of Yuyao, made a living by drying salt and was relatively well-off. At midnight on the 31st of last month, five or six bandits suddenly came, broke down the door with pistols in hand, and searched wildly. They also tied up Jinyun and demanded five hundred yuan. After Jinyun knelt on the ground and begged, he borrowed from all sides and managed to raise the sum. The bandits got the money and released Ying and fled to the northeast.

Xiaoshan 84

New Prices for New Flue-Cured Tobacco: New flue-cured tobacco has come on the market in Xiaoshao Guali Kanshan sandy land. Due to the wind and rain disasters recently, the late planting has suffered losses. The industry decided by the Anchang Flue-Cured Tobacco Industry Association that the price is fifteen yuan and four jiao per hundred catties (sixteen tael scale). The market still needs to see an increase. In addition, the flue-cured tobacco in the four western townships this year's harvest season is very poor, and due to the hot weather and more rain than sun, most of it cannot be dried and is mostly moldy. It has been reported that the market price of new tobacco is from fifteen yuan to eighteen yuan, and there is no good product.

Hefei 85

Another Major Fire at Ximatang: Ding's grocery store at Ximatang, the Sixth Girls' Middle School, caught fire at 4 PM on the 26th due to frying peanuts. The fire immediately spread to the roof and affected the home of Li Zihe to the east, and also spread to the neighbors. Fortunately, the fire was put out by the fire hydrants and the Public Security Bureau. It is estimated that twenty to thirty houses were burned, totaling about eighty rooms. Several of the families had moved here after the previous major fire in the west gate, which is truly unfortunate.

Temporary Relief Committee for Flood Disasters Established: The flooding in Jiangbei Xingdong counties has been severe. Local figures have organized a temporary relief committee for the flood disasters in Jiangbei, with Leng Yuqiu as the chairman and Lu Xiaobo as the vice-chairman.

Letter Received

Letter from All Police Officers of the Fourth Precinct of Songjiang County 86

Respected Editor: The news articles "The patrol captain surrounds the district chief to demand salary" and "Details of insulting the district chief" that were published in your newspaper on the 30th and 31st of last month are completely inconsistent with the facts. Upon reading them, we were deeply surprised. The police salaries of the Fourth Precinct of Songjiang City have always been allocated from the housing police donations collected by the First District Office and paid out on the 10th of the following month. Everything has been in order. However, since June, the salaries have been delayed until the 25th of the following month. For the police officers, their salaries are used for living expenses. Every time the salary is due, they are looking forward to it like a drought expecting rain. Unexpectedly, the police salaries for July were delayed until August 25th and were still not paid out. The police officers heard that the housing police donations for July had already been collected, and those for August had also been collected. Therefore, they asked the police inspector and the bureau chief to repeatedly request the payment. However, District Chief Zhong Taishi ignored them. Later, the county magistrate ordered the salaries to be paid quickly, but he still ignored the order. On August 29th, the police inspector had no money to cover the meals, and all the police officers were on the verge of starvation. The police inspector had no choice but to go to the District Office again to urge the payment. However, District Chief Zhong was angered by the police inspector's repeated urgings and slammed the table, yelling, "What are you? How dare you speak?" The police inspector returned without any results. He told the police officers about the situation. The police officers believed that District Chief Zhong would not be so unreasonable and unconcerned for his subordinates. They were still suspicious. Later, on the suggestion of everyone, several patrol captains were elected to accompany the police inspector to the District Office to verify the situation. When they went, the police inspector still politely requested District Chief Zhong. The patrol captains had received training and strictly maintained order when disbursing funds. They did not dare to say anything outrageous. In the end, no money was paid out. On the contrary, the District Office falsely accused the patrol captains of insulting the district chief to the County Government and the Public Security Bureau. The patrol captains are of low status and small jobs and could not do anything. They only feel that the administrative staff under the Party rule are still overbearing and sigh with emotion. It should be known that the police salaries are borne by all the merchants and residents of the city, but the District Office collects and disburses them. Other than a dozen districts, all districts do the same. We have not heard of anyone failing to pay the police salaries clearly until the third month. As of yesterday (September 2nd), the salaries had still not been paid out. Now, your newspaper publishes Zhong District Chief's solo responsibilities in the house police donations and how he contributed to the allocations. This kind of statement seems to imply that the police salaries are maintained by Zhong District Chief personally. It is also said that he has accumulated nearly two thousand gold coins. According to the budget revenue and expenditure, it was approved by the county-wide administrative meeting and reported for approval. There is no shortage. Even if there is such a thing, why did Zhong District Chief not apply to the County Government for remedy earlier? Now the sudden cut off of the police officers' living expenses is so handled, how can it be said to be legal? The above situation has long been publicly evaluated by various agencies and local figures in Songyi. There is no need to argue. However, because your newspaper's reporting is inaccurate, we will briefly describe the situation and facts. We have always known that your newspaper's public opinion is fair and does not damage its reputation due to personal feelings. We hope you will publish it in the "Letters to the Editor" section to clarify the truth. The police officers of the Fourth Precinct of Songjiang County, together, September 3.
