Lianyi Society and Other Non-Employee Organizations 133

May Not Represent Laborers

Various stores, factories, and shop assistants in this city have had trade union organizations as powerful groups representing their respective people. Since the central government explicitly ordered their dissolution, most of these groups have been reorganized into Lianyi Societies, Lianshan Associations, etc. Those that have already been prepared for organization include the Nanhuo (Southern Goods) Industry Employee Lianyi Society and the China Electric Company Employee Lianyi Society. All have been permitted to be established by the Municipal Party Department and should register with the competent authorities according to the regulations before they can be formally established. It is reported that the Social Bureau has examined their nature and found them similar to disguised trade unions, and has specifically sent a letter to the Municipal People's Training Association to explain their nature and stipulate their powers to avoid disputes. Yesterday, a reply was received from the Municipal Party Department, stating that Lianyi Societies, etc., are mutual aid organizations for factory staff or store assistants to connect feelings and increase knowledge. The intention is good and should be protected, but their nature is social groups, not professional groups, and they cannot represent laborers. If they exceed this scope, they should be corrected. The Social Bureau immediately issued an order to the Lianyi Societies, etc., to handle matters in accordance with the regulations for supervising social groups in this city.

Social Bureau Continues to Recruit Factory Inspectors 134

The first class of students from the Factory Inspector Training Institute run by the Ministry of Industry has graduated on the 3rd of this month. The ten people sent by the Shanghai Social Bureau have already arrived at the bureau to serve, and the second phase of training will begin on the 15th of this month. The Municipal Social Bureau still needs to continue to recruit five or six trainees. A stipend will be given during the training period, and the monthly salary after graduation will start from 80 yuan. Qualifications for application require graduation from a specialized school at or above the national or international level, with a diploma, or equivalent academic qualifications. Alternatively, applicants must have worked in a factory for ten years, possess considerable academic skills, and obtain proof from the factory. The examination subjects are the Party's ideology, Chinese language, foreign language (English, or both French and Japanese), an overview of economics, labor issues, mathematics (algebra), physics, and mechanics, as well as a physical examination. The registration dates are from September 5th to 10th. When registering, applicants must submit two recent four-inch half-length photographs and a diploma or certificate. The examination dates are September 11th and 12th. The registration and examination locations are both at the Social Bureau on Zhonghua Road.

Dispute Between Hotel Staff and Boatmen Resolved 135

The receptionists of the Shanghai Hotel Industry Association and the boatmen of the United Office for Luggage Transport in the Huangpu River have had disputes in business, and the two sides have attacked each other fiercely. In order to resolve the situation quickly, the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Social Bureau, and Public Utilities Bureau convened both parties for a trial mediation on the afternoon of the day before yesterday. Zhang Shouchun and Huang Zuna of the Public Security Bureau, Zhang Shuye and Chen Zeyi of the Social Bureau, Gao Shuan of the Public Utilities Bureau, Zhang Yukun and Xiong Guangcai of the Hotel Reception Workers' Union, and Fei Wanhong, Huang Bujin, and Lu Guangtong of the boatmen attended. As a result, the following measures were decided: (A) Since the boatmen have been registered by the Public Security Bureau, the receptionists cannot treat them as unregistered boatmen as before. Therefore, in the future, when passengers' luggage is received, it must be handed over to the boatmen for transport. (B) Boatmen are not allowed to solicit customers on board or hook onto ships. (C) Boatmen are only allowed to transport goods on the ship. When transported to the pier, they should hand over the luggage to the receptionists and are not allowed to carry the luggage to the hotel. The receptionists are also not allowed to force the boatmen to send the luggage to the hotel. (D) Pier fees are blackmail by gangsters and should not be paid in the future. If gangsters forcibly demand them, both parties can report to the Public Security Bureau for arrest. (E) The various malpractices of hotels exploiting receptionists will be detailed in a petition by the receptionists for rectification.

County Government Held a Police Affairs Meeting Yesterday 137

The Shanghai County Government convened a police affairs meeting yesterday. The heads of the six Public Security Bureaus, Zhang Xingbang, Zhao Lian, Zhu Xiangcheng, Zhang Zhenyuan, Xiao Jianxun, and Wu Shizhao, as well as Yao Fusheng, the head of the County Government's Public Security Section, and Chief Inspector Xu Yi, attended. The meeting was chaired by Yao Fusheng and recorded by Hu Gongshou. At the beginning of the meeting, the chairman reported that he was convening the meeting today on behalf of the county magistrate and chairman. Recently, according to the report of the chief inspector, the inspection of the on-duty situation of various sub-bureaus in late August was carried out, and each item was instructed to be corrected, and the county magistrate approved each point, and the heads of each sub-bureau were notified to pay attention to compliance. In addition, the bad habits of the police in this county are still few, and it is relatively easy to rectify them. However, the number of illiterate people is relatively large, and training is not without difficulty. Each sub-bureau chief should always find ways to make them learn. The police have heavy responsibilities, and all administrative facilities are closely related to the police. It is hoped that colleagues will rise up and work hard to rectify. There are great hopes for the future of police affairs in this county. Next, Chief Inspector Xu reported that he was reporting the actual situation found during the inspection and never involved emotional factors. Eliminating feelings and striving to thoroughly rectify police administration has always been a cautious plan. It is hoped that the heads of each sub-bureau will pay attention to it. After the report, the Public Security Section proposed various cases: (1) The division of patrol areas. As a result, each sub-bureau divided the patrol areas according to the local terrain and submitted a map with the route drawn by the 15th of this month. On the one hand, the county will investigate the recent census and household registration surveys in Qingxiang and copy the number of households in each township to each sub-bureau for reference. (2) Strictly restrict the case of apprentice police officers graduating from the Changjing supplementary school requesting to be dismissed. As a result, it was passed as is, but the county government should stipulate reward and punishment methods and notify them for compliance. (3) The winter defense should be prepared early. As a result, it was passed as is, but the census cards of the villagers should be recorded and notified to the public offices in each district, and transferred to the township heads to cooperate and handle the implementation of personnel registration. The county government will notify the residents to strictly comply. (4) The technical training of Changjing should be actively carried out. As a result, (A) it will be handled accordingly, (B) the time and curriculum will be listed and submitted to each sub-bureau for review. (5) How to remedy the illiterate Changjing officers? As a result, the county government issued police answers as teaching materials. Zhu, head of the third sub-bureau, proposed an interim proposal regarding how to stipulate the problem of Changjing's guarantor. As a result, (A) the county government supplements the guarantor; (B) the head of each sub-bureau is responsible for obtaining the guarantor for the applicant of each sub-bureau; (C) from today onwards, the old police officers will be jointly guaranteed by five police officers from the same bureau.

The Shanghai Real Estate Association held a membership meeting yesterday at 4:00 PM, with more than 30 people attending. Kui Yanfang was elected chairman and Tao Rongqin was the recorder. Reader's Letter

Letter from Ms. Su Fen

Fen was forced by the environment to drop out of school. She has been out of school for many years and is very sad. Now she wants to go to society to find some jobs to slightly reduce her mental pain. However, because of her shallow knowledge, she doesn't know where to find a job or what kind of job is suitable for her. She is also unfamiliar with the place, so she doesn't dare to move forward. Yesterday, she read the reader's letter column of Shen Bao and was very comforted. Kind gentlemen, what kind of place needs someone like me who has no strength and can only write? What kind of job is suitable for me? I sincerely ask for your guidance.

(Reply) I am sorry you are asking about the direction of finding a job, but you did not explain what you have learned before and to what extent you dropped out of school, nor did you explain your current environment. I am afraid that my reply will not be very pertinent.

It is best to have considerable preparation before finding a job. Looking at the level of writing in your letter, you may be able to handle document copying and letter drafting with some effort. However, the more ordinary your ability is, the more difficult it is to find a job. If you have the opportunity, you should further improve your writing skills, which will naturally be easier to achieve your goal. Formal schooling is certainly not easy, or you may want to consider a kind of tutoring or self-study that does not interfere with family duties. Are there any tutoring schools nearby? Are there any teachers who can guide self-study? Are there any classmates or other friends who can help you guide you and solve this problem? I still hope that you can think about it more on your own. We do not know you in detail and cannot give you a concrete answer. I hope you will forgive me.

However, I have a word to offer you. Those who have the will succeed, especially in youth. The future is full of opportunities. There are more hopes. Since you are determined to serve society, you can find the ideal realm through the possible environment in a roundabout way. It is not a very difficult thing. The most needed are clear and reasonable opinions and the courage to fight peacefully. The most undesirable things are pessimism and recklessness.

Shen Bao Reader's Letter Regulations 151

The staff of this newspaper firmly believe that readers have several personal problems that need to be discussed urgently. Based on the spirit of serving society, the staff are willing to act as consultants and try to discuss matters in writing with the utmost sincerity. If readers can obtain appropriate solutions, reduce some difficulties, and increase some happiness, it will be a great pleasure.

1. For the time being, the problems that you want to discuss with the staff of this newspaper are limited to the three items of schooling, occupation, and marriage.

2. When communicating, please first state your name, gender, age, occupation (or school, grade), native place, and mailing address (it is still advisable to open in detail when continuing to communicate, for fear that the previous letter may not reach). After that, state the problems you want to discuss. The text should be detailed, accurate, and easy for people to understand the true meaning. Please write "Shen Bao Reader's Letter Department" on the outside of the envelope and attach a corresponding amount of return postage stamps.

3. When communicating, you must cut out the stamp printed on the special issue of this newspaper's reader's letter column and stick it on the upper left corner of the stationery as a voucher.

4. The processing method after this newspaper receives the letter: A. Respect the reader's intention. All letters that state that they wish not to be answered in the newspaper or do not want to disclose their names when answering will be followed. B. If the letter does not state how to answer, but the staff think that answering one person has value for everyone to refer to, it should be disclosed in the newspaper.

C. If the letter states that it hopes to be answered in the newspaper, but it is limited by the length of the article, it can only be disclosed selectively, or it may not be disclosed, or the disclosure has to be delayed due to the problem still being under consideration. Please forgive me, but if it cannot be answered in the newspaper, it will still be answered by mail.

▲ Correction: The news that Lin Xiangxiang, a sedan driver, was burned to death in the home of the famous doctor Xia Yingtang, which was reported in the newspaper yesterday and the day before yesterday, was found to have occurred in the jurisdiction of the First Sub-Bureau of the Second District. This newspaper mistakenly reported it as the Second Sub-Bureau of the First District. This is a special correction.

Education News

Special Feature

The Effect of Supplementary Education is Where? 154

By Jiang Wenyu (3)

If we want to teach this group of lovable young people currently in the workforce, ensuring each can increase their occupational productivity, we should certainly give them the opportunity for supplementary education. Moreover, if we want to teach them to serve faithfully, love their community and country, and aspire to progress, we cannot but rely on supplementary education. Another point is that we truly hope that a majority of young people who graduate from elementary school or junior high school are willing to serve in the workforce. Therefore, there should be extremely perfect and substantial supplementary education institutions, so that they have a place to study and a path to advancement. On one hand, they can study with peace of mind, and on the other hand, they can work hard to pursue learning, so that their skills improve through learning, and their learning advances further due to having a job. We need not criticize China's current education system and methods, but the eight characters "(not very suitable, in urgent need of remedy)" are probably acknowledged by everyone.

First, it can teach the public to not spend a lot of money. To set up a school, in any case, one must build school buildings and purchase teaching equipment. However, wouldn't it be a great pity if a towering and grand school building with splendid and complete teaching equipment is locked up and unused after students finish classes at four o'clock in the afternoon? Now, by borrowing existing schools to implement supplementary education, there is no need for additional equipment. If industrial schools are used for industrial supplementary education, the advantage is even greater. There are four and a half hours from 5:00 PM to 9:30 PM every day. If there are two classes per two hours, two levels can be set up in one classroom. Teachers are certainly very tired if they work all day long, but those with extraordinary energy and enthusiasm for education may be able to concurrently hold this position. The salary of these part-time teachers is naturally lower than that of daytime teachers, so a lot of money is saved. The public spends less money, but education reaches more people. How economical is this? (If worker supplementary schools are established in large factories and are run successfully, the government should provide even more rewards.) Second, it can teach society to increase productivity and enhance national survival. A majority of young people in the workforce can collectively receive occupational training to refine their skills and expand their capabilities. The improvement of individual production skills and the increase in production quantity, when gathered together, will result in the improvement of the entire country's and society's production skills and the increase in production quantity. In this way, can't the difficult problems of national poverty and people's poverty be mostly solved? Not only that, but as mentioned earlier, supplementary education has three major pillars (namely, physical education and military-civilian training, as well as personality and moral cultivation, in addition to vocational training). These are even more important conditions for the expression of national survival and are especially necessary for China, which is accumulating poverty and weakness. If a majority of young people can increase their production capacity through supplementary education, and can also unite as a group, be of one heart and mind, love their country, and strive diligently, the foundation of the country will naturally be extremely consolidated, and the future of the nation will also gain infinite glory.

Third, it can teach a majority of young people who are unable to continue their studies to obtain opportunities for further education. Therefore, they will not suffer from employment but will enjoy it. Young people who enter the workforce often regret not being able to further their studies. This is also a common human sentiment and can be said to be a manifestation of young people's desire for advancement (but a portion of those who are influenced by the corrupting effects of the imperial examination system and regard graduating from university as a mere decoration should certainly be excluded). Now, there is supplementary education to meet their needs. They work during the day and study at night. Credits are divided into multiple levels, progressing step by step. It is not difficult to reach university from middle school. With ten years of hard work and no financial reward, their knowledge and skills can actually be equal to those of high school and vocational school graduates (even if not entirely complete, at least a portion is the same as the result of higher education). In this way, the majority of young people in the workforce can be jubilant and no longer suffer from employment. Not only will they not suffer, but because they can study with peace of mind after employment, avoiding the burden of tuition fees for their parents and enduring hardship, they will realize that their personal future is bright and splendid, or even be overjoyed. In this way, these young people, and even the fathers and brothers of young people, can gradually change their past special psychology (such as the psychology of valuing further education and favoring vanity, the psychology of looking down on occupations and valuing knowledge, and the psychology of doubting current education and disliking current schools). At this time, education that has reached a dead end can gain a great turning point.

The above are all visible and obvious effects. As for the special effectiveness that supplementary education can demonstrate in promoting compulsory education and subsidizing vocational education under China's special social circumstances, there is no need to say more.

The China Vocational Education Society has been researching and implementing supplementary education for many years. Its affiliated institutions include morning schools, evening schools, and correspondence courses. Although it is not possible to achieve the level of (three pillars standing together and five levels fully equipped) at once, the society's colleagues have long harbored the great aspiration to complete supplementary education and develop supplementary education. Recently, the Society's office has newly added a supplementary education department in order to concentrate efforts, unify affairs, experiment with research, and advance on multiple paths. We sincerely hope to earnestly connect and work together with colleagues in the education and vocational fields to jointly plan and advance, so that China's future supplementary education can become an important stronghold in the education field and a good remedy for curing education's illnesses. Because I am a person serving in the Vocational Education Society and have a special interest in supplementary education, I dare to briefly describe my feelings in order to seek correction from colleagues at home and abroad (End)

Written on August 24th, the twentieth year of the Republic of China, at the office of the China Vocational Education Society

Important News

Jiangsu Education Department Urges Hu Huanyong to Take Office as Principal of Suzhou Middle School 155

Suzhou Middle School of Jiangsu Province was originally formed by the merger of the Second Middle School and the First Normal School. Its foundation is solid and its scale is large. Since Principal Wang Maozu took over, its achievements have been remarkable. Recently, Jiang, the concurrent principal of the Central Political School, cordially invited Wang to be the director of the Education Department of the school. Wang decided to resign from the position of principal of Suzhou Middle School out of a sense of duty. The Jiangsu Education Department repeatedly tried to persuade him to stay to no avail and has approved his resignation. The seat of principal of Suzhou Middle School that he left behind has been submitted to the provincial government for discussion. It was decided at the meeting to appoint Hu Huanyong as the replacement. According to reports, Hu is a graduate of the former National Nanjing Higher Normal School and Southeast University. After leaving school, he served as a history and geography teacher and concurrently as a dean of discipline in the former Jiangsu Eighth Middle School and First Middle School for many years. Later, because he aspired to further his studies, he studied geography and meteorology in France at his own expense. After returning to China, he successively served as a researcher and secretary at the Meteorological Research Institute of the National Central Research Institute, and as an adjunct associate professor at the National Central University. He is currently an associate professor and head of the Geography Department of the College of Science at Central University. His knowledge and experience are both very extensive. However, it is heard that Hu still humbly declines. Yesterday, the Jiangsu Education Department, with the start of the school term approaching, not only telegraphed Hu to take office as soon as possible but also specially dispatched Xiang Shaoxuan.

Local News

Meeting of the Poor Education Foundation 159

Preparing to Recruit the Second Batch of Scholarship Students

The Poor Education Foundation Committee convened its autumn general meeting at the Bankers' Association the other day, in accordance with its charter. The following committee members attended: Cao Huiqun, Xu Shanxiang, Xu Peizan, Xu Zuohe, Xu Mingcai, Zhang Yiyun, Shen Enfu, Jiang Weiqiao, Song Wusheng, Hu Shuhua, Cheng Yingzhang, and founder Wu Yun. More than ten people were present. Chairman Cao Huiqun first reported that the first recruitment of scholarship students was conducted with the most open attitude and the fairest method, selecting 14 students who have now been sent to National Central University, Chekiang University, and Datong University. In addition to the Foundation covering their tuition, board, and miscellaneous fees, the students' pocket money is also issued by the Foundation, so that each scholarship student can study with peace of mind and not have their efforts distracted by raising funds. Next, Wu Yunchu proposed methods for raising the number of scholarships, explaining that the Foundation's funds are only over ten thousand yuan, which is not a large amount. This time, individual donations of monthly salaries were used to raise 14 scholarships. If no other avenues are found next year, it may be difficult to recruit scholarship students for the second batch. After discussion, the committee members passed the following principles: (1) The Foundation will raise a certain number of scholarships each year to subsidize graduates of junior high school and above who enter universities or vocational schools. (2) Each scholarship will cost 300 yuan per year, and its duration will depend on the major and school designated by the donor. (3) Donors are welcome to recognize one-quarter, one-half, a full scholarship, or multiple scholarships. (4) For those who recognize a full scholarship, the donor's name will be added to the scholarship to increase visual appeal and show that they are not forgotten. Those who recognize a certain number of scholarships or more may, in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Education, apply for commendation. (5) For those who recognize half a scholarship or less, the scholarship will be named after the surnames of the donors, with appropriate consideration. (6) It is preferred that donations be paid in full at once, but they may also be paid annually. It is heard that although about ten scholarships have been recognized, the large number of students taking the exam this year seems to exceed what ten scholarships can accommodate, so they will continue to actively seek recognition of scholarships from those with enthusiasm for education in order to promote poor education.

Shanghai South Zhabei Municipal Elementary Schools Raise Funds to Help with Disaster Relief 160

The Shanghai South Zhabei Municipal Elementary Schools Fund Raising Committee for Disaster Relief held its first meeting at the Feihong Elementary School. The following attended: Chen Pin Yi, Feng Xi Wu, Xu Zi Hua, Zhang Xiao Tian, Li Bo Jun, Qian Xuan Qing, Zhao Lu Qing. The following matters were resolved: (1) Discussing the date for each school to submit the funds: It was decided to be from September 5th to September 15th. (2) Discussing the date and location for each school to submit the funds: It was decided that each school should submit all funds raised to the Shanghai Bank at the West Gate in Nanshi or the Shanghai Bank at the Boundary Road in Beishi before September 20th, and report the total amount of funds to the Committee (Chen Pin Yi of Feihong Elementary School) for statistics. (3) Discussing the scope of fundraising for each school: It was decided that the scope of fundraising for each school should be limited to the staff and students of the school and their families, streets, and public places. They vowed not to participate in anything else. (4) Discussing the amount of fundraising: It was decided to follow the standards set by the Shanghai Education Community Flood Relief Joint Meeting, with students donating at least two jiao each, teachers and staff donating three times the amount of students, and students' families donating freely. However, they may make changes based on the situation. (5) Discussing how to prepare the receipt booklets needed for the funds raised by each school: It was decided that the Committee would draft a style and notify each school to print it according to the style and add the bureau-issued school seal (on the two connected margins) before using it (style attached later). (6) Discussing how to prepare the fundraising notices and publicity materials for each school: It was decided that each school would handle it themselves, but they must send a copy to the Committee for future editing of the report. (7) Discussing who would contact the Shanghai Bank at the West Gate and the Boundary Road: It was decided that Xu Zihua and Chen Pin Yi would be responsible.

Preparations for Labor Children's Schools are Ready 161

Established in Key Areas of Various Factories

Books Supplied and Tuition Waived

The Labor Education Committee of this city, in view of the importance of labor education, decided through its first meeting to establish a number of labor children's schools starting this semester. The funds will be disbursed from the interest earned from the Labor Education Fund, and all books and supplies will be provided by the school free of charge. It is heard that people with rich experience in labor education have been sought in Wusong, Yangshupu, Zhabei, Caojiadu, Pudong, and other factory areas. They will hold a discussion meeting at the Municipal Party Headquarters on September 2 to discuss the implementation plan. Our hardworking laborers, who support themselves by the sweat of their brows, can reduce the burden of tuition fees for their children. This is truly a blessing for the laborers.

County Township Normal School to Establish Simple Elementary School 164

Starting this semester, the Shanghai County Rural Normal School will establish a simple elementary school in this town for the students of the school to practice teaching. The simple elementary school is specially designed for out-of-school children. Classes are taught for two hours each day, divided into morning and afternoon shifts. It can enroll more than 100 students. Poor children who are usually occupied with household chores or work to earn a meager profit and have no time to study will have the opportunity to receive education. The school site is located at the Chenghuang Temple in Hedong, and the principal has been determined to be Zhang Yongqing, a graduate of the first class of the Township Normal School.

Two Important Notices from Shanghai Foreign Football Club 168

Annual General Meeting to be Held on Thursday, September 10th

Important Rule Changes Regarding Throw-Ins and Three Other Items

The Shanghai Foreign Football Club issued two important notices yesterday: (1) The annual general meeting will be held on September 10th. (2) Important competition rules have been changed. The details are as follows:

Holding the Annual General Meeting 169

Five Important Proposals

The notice of the annual general meeting states: To all members: The annual general meeting of the Shanghai Foreign Football Club is now scheduled to be held at the auditorium of the Church School at No. 21 Jiujiang Road at 5:00 PM on Thursday, September 10th. The important proposals are listed below:

▲Acceptance of Minutes: Whether to accept the minutes of the previous annual general meeting held on Thursday, September 11, 1930, as recorded, if there are no errors

▲Acceptance of Reports: Whether to accept the Secretary's report for the last season of 1930-31 as appropriate and the Treasurer's financial report as accurate and correct

▲Election of Officers: Election of important officers for this term of 1931-32: (1) President (2) Vice President (3) Honorary Secretary (4) Three events designated by Rule 6 (not representatives of each team on the Council) (5) Other officers

▲Amendment of the Charter: Proposal by Hemsen, seconded by Blofarth, whether to amend Article 21 of the Charter as follows: (Article 21: Team Transfers - Players may transfer from Team A to Team B, but only once per season. Under very special circumstances, after three months from the start of each league season, transfers may be approved by the Executive Committee of the General Assembly)

▲Other Business: Other miscellaneous matters concerning the General Assembly

Notice of Rule Changes

The Secretary of the General Assembly announced the following changes to the rules of football matches, as notified by the London Football Association:

▲Rule 5 (Original): When the ball goes out of bounds, the opposing team member of the one who caused it to go out of bounds shall throw it in from the line at the point where it went out of bounds. The player throwing the ball must stand with both feet outside the line and facing the field, throwing it with both hands over the head in any direction. A goal scored directly from a throw-in does not count. The thrower may only touch the ball after another thrower touches it. (Correction): After "(throwing it in any direction)," add "(If the above throwing rules are violated, it will be changed to the other party throwing it)." At the end of the rule, add "(If this part of the rule is violated (that is, the ball is touched immediately without touching another player), the other party will be awarded a free kick.)"

▲Rule 11 (Original): A winning goal scored from a corner kick counts. A free kick awarded for a violation of Rule 9, if directly kicked into a winning goal, counts. However, other free kicks are not included in this example. (Correction): (The position of the second half of the sentence is slightly changed and should be translated as) A free kick directly kicked into the goal by such a violation counts as a winning goal for the non-offending team.

▲Definition 4 (Original): Goalkeeper: Walking with the ball for no more than two steps. (Correction): (Two steps) is changed to (Four steps). The above rule changes have been approved by the International Football Council on June 13, 1931.

Free Discussion

Not Removing Garden Weeds, Discussions by Zhai Fu

The Three Classes of People in the World 170

There are three classes of people in the world. The first class follows the brain as the commander; the second class follows the stomach as the commander; the third class follows the reproductive organs as the commander. The natural part that each person follows as the commander is the thermometer of his personality. We should stand under the banner of whichever commander we want to be. I propose this view not with the hope that everyone will become immortals who do not eat the smoke of the world or self-knowledge monastics. Even Kant, who emphasized the life of reason, wanted to find a lover twice. Bo Yi and Shu Qi also had to eat before King Wu attacked Zhou. I am not advocating that the brain should come out to sever the two desires of food and sex, but rather that the brain should come out to take responsibility for command. Generally, people sometimes listen to the brain's command, sometimes listen to the stomach's command, and sometimes listen to the reproductive organs' command. When he is commanded by the stomach and reproductive organs, he becomes dizzy and unable to extricate himself. Some people, all day long, all year round, all their lives, are fighting for food and love, forgetting everything, willingly becoming food-obsessed and love-crazed, and never waking up until they die; such people are the most pitiful. Young friends! Now the brain, stomach, and reproductive organs are all starting to recruit soldiers. Establish your purpose, recognize your banner, and choose your commander to serve!

Electric Eyes at the Entrance of American Theaters 171

— Li Zhiqing

There is a United Artists Theater in Chicago, USA. Recently, a new invention has been installed that can automatically register the number of audience members entering the theater. It is said that the United Artists Theater is the first theater in Chicago to use this new invention. Currently, it is only for testing purposes. If the results are remarkable after testing, then all theaters in the United States will follow suit and compete to install it. This can be asserted.

This new invention is called "electric eyes" by everyone. Its construction principle is to use a kind of light to illuminate the entrance of the theater. However, this light is not visible to the naked eye. Every time a person passes through it, the light will show a wave. The number of audience members can be inferred from the number of waves. Therefore, theaters that want to install this new invention must specially set up gates at their entrances so that the audience can line up in a single file and enter one after another, so that the light waves will not be disturbed. Every time the light passes through a wave, the counter in the theater manager's office automatically counts. The shape of this counter is like the counter on a foreign taxi. The counting ranges from one to nine thousand nine hundred and ninety-nine, following the arithmetic addition method completely.

Therefore, theater managers, with this new invention, only need to look at the counter at any time to know how many audience members have arrived up to a certain time. If someone is operating several theaters in one place at the same time, they only need to connect their general office to each theater with wires and install separate counters. Then the business status of each theater can be seen at a glance every minute. Expanding on this, if someone is operating several theaters in various places at the same time, they only need to connect to the general office with wires and install separate counters. At any time, they can know the business status of theaters in various places. What could be more beneficial?

However, this electric eye, in addition to being able to immediately report the business status, can also prevent ticket sellers and ticket takers from engaging in fraud. Because from now on, the ticket price and the number of free tickets for each show in the theater must match the number of people reported on the counter. Otherwise, the theater authorities will only question the ticket sellers and ticket takers.

A Word of Advice 172

Friendship between people depends on mutual admiration and need. When one side's conditions disappear, the friendship ceases. In discussing friendship, the ancients and moderns alike first mention Guan Zhong and Bao Shuya. It must be understood that Bao Shuya's righteousness was certainly high, but his discernment was even more unattainable. This is because he would not divide gold unless it was with Guan Zhong. If the recipient of the gold was not Guan Zhong, he would not have become Bao Shuya. Today's enthusiasts of socialising only blame others for not being Bao Shuya, but do not blame themselves for not being Guan Zhong. Why not think more deeply about this?

▲The purest form of love should not have conditions, like food. The habit of enjoying scabs is something one might keep for life. People are unlikely to question why one enjoys sweet flag and jujubes. This is how things can remain unchanged over time. Otherwise, even delicacies become tiresome, let alone simple fare. Moreover, once there are conditions, there are comparisons and changes. This is the result of free love, which is why there are so many divorces. However, have the talented scholars and beautiful women of old not been free? Has their love not been without conditions? One must understand that it actually stemmed from a feeling of cherishing talent. Talent is something unchanging and imperishable, unlike money and status, which can be gained, lost, and change. Therefore, the stories of Hong Fu and Zhuo Wenjun have become timeless tales of romance (Dream Butterfly).

Brief Notes on Painting Lessons at the Huifeng Studio 173

— Chen Meng'an

Kuang Junyou from Lingui is the eldest son of the late Mr. Huifeng. He inherited his family's scholarship and has long been known for his talent. He excelled in his studies from a young age and once sought advice from such elders as Jiang Yingsheng Yun, He Pansou Weipu, and Wu Canlu Junqing. These elders all valued him highly. Having studied diligently, his achievements grew with age. Kuang Junyou was born in Wanxian, Sichuan. Guilin's landscape is the best in the world, and it is also Kuang Junyou's hometown. Endowed with natural beauty, he is uniquely blessed. Moreover, he has seen many genuine works of the ancients and has copied them extensively. He has achieved perfection in both natural talent and academic ability. Therefore, his brushwork is different from that of contemporary historians. Kuang Junyou often creates original drafts for his paintings. He often stretches paper and holds a brush amidst banquets and gatherings, completing them in a moment. His work is lush, vibrant, and vigorous, and his spirit meets with the ancients. If one has not deeply studied the past, how can one speak of this? Recently, during the summer heat, he used painting as a pastime during breaks from his studies. His inspired thoughts flew quickly, resulting in many excellent works. Zhu Zhang Qiangcun, Cheng Zhang Shifa, and many famous figures at sea have seen them and admired them greatly. Many have added poems and inscriptions, making the beautiful paintings and famous calligraphy even more outstanding. Yesterday, I visited his Xiaohuifeng Studio and saw him engaged in the task of mixing lead and grinding powder. As a result, I was able to have a comprehensive view of his works. Besides landscapes, there were also flowers, plants, and Buddhist images. He imitated the ancients and created his own works, each extremely exquisite. Large and small scrolls filled the walls, making one sigh in admiration. This is not out of personal favouritism. Among them, two paintings were particularly outstanding. Kuang Junyou once obtained old paper and cut it into a small scroll, only an inch high and over ten feet long. One was a small album of three-inch squares. Both were landscapes, with thousands of peaks and valleys, and misty waters. They captured the essence of a thousand miles in a small space. Zhang Qiang and others wrote inscriptions for them, knowing that their discerning eyes would not be mistaken. Kuang Junyou paints to relieve the summer heat, mainly for his own enjoyment. Friends who saw it urged him to display it publicly to share it with others. Kuang Junyou, respecting the wishes of the crowd and also wanting to seek corrections from the masters, specially opened an exhibition at the Ningbo Native Place Association for three days. It opens today. Jia Li, Qian Furen, is skilled in cursive script. Her wise younger brother, Xiao Song, is proficient in imitating seals and making inscriptions. The whole family is refined and elegant, carrying on the beauty of their predecessors. We know that the legacy of our teacher will last forever.

Anecdotes of Disaster Relief 174

— Huai

The children's music composer, Mr. Hu Jingxi, deeply moved by the deaths caused by the floods and realizing the need for publicity to raise funds for disaster relief, has specially composed three "Begging for Relief" songs. The lyrics are as follows: (1) "The wind whistles, the rain is heavy, the river water rises endlessly. The dam has collapsed and cannot be repaired. The embankment has broken and the water flows horizontally. Endless and boundless is the water, with tens of thousands of families grieving to heaven and earth. The wind whistles, the rain is heavy, regretting not being a carp that can swim." (2) "Regret is long, tears are thick, flooding fields and submerging high-rise buildings. People and objects float with the waves. Millions of disaster victims are like prisoners of Chu. Becoming orphans and widows, where to drift? No food and clothing, worry before our eyes. Regret is long, tears are thick, and winter is coming, colder with no fur coat." (3) "Cry sadly, beg bitterly, donate generously to the disaster relief fund. Send clothes and pants, distribute grain and food. Saving lives is more meritorious than building a Buddha temple. How can we bear not to save those in danger? Who will we turn to when we are in danger? Cry sadly, beg bitterly, compatriots quickly raise the relief fund." It is reported that these songs have been widely spread in various schools as teaching materials, and children's saving for snacks will be used to help with disaster relief. This will have a considerable impact. It is hoped that various schools will widely promote it.

The Shanghai Runyu storytelling troupe, it is rumoured that on the 5th of this month, there will be a voluntary storytelling event. The money earned from the storytelling will be used for flood disaster relief. The Shanghai-based members of the Suzhou Guangyu troupe will also hold a similar event. A meeting was held at the Oriental Bookstore on Tibet Road on the morning of the day before yesterday at 11:00 a.m. After discussion, the manager of the bookstore, Chen Yin Chun, agreed to hold a special storytelling event on the 9th and 10th. In the evening, amateur theatrical performances will be added to attract audiences. Tickets will be sold for half a yuan each. The Oriental Bookstore will not deduct any expenses. All miscellaneous backstage expenses will be borne by the members of the troupe. However, after a public vote, it was decided to use the troupe's public funds for this purpose. Furthermore, the original plan was to be realistic and not sell additional tickets. The total ticket price earned from the four sessions day and night on those two days would be handed over to the disaster relief agencies for distribution. However, due to concerns from some people that the appeal might be weak, it was still proposed to print tickets and sell them door-to-door. Although those responsible for selling the tickets were very enthusiastic, the ticket price was one yuan per ticket. It was stated at the time that tickets would be collected on the 9th and the money would be handed over to the disaster relief effort on the evening of the 10th to finalize the matter. If it is possible to completely get rid of the long-standing habit of selling voluntary tickets door-to-door and quickly finalize the matter, it would be a new record in the history of fundraising. However, it is feared that it will be difficult to escape the long-standing habits. However, according to the reports from those responsible for selling the tickets, everyone is very confident. It is believed that it will not repeat the old mistakes.

Records of Things Seen and Heard in the Old Capital 175

— Zhuan

Flowering Cherry

A guest does not like Beijing, saying that the dust in Beijing rises to the sky in spring and summer, choking the mouth and nose. Chewing it makes a sound. How can this be tolerated? I responded that it is indeed true. There are more than one aspects of Beijing's municipal administration that need to be discussed. This is one of them. In the future, if the municipal authorities can open up larger-scale projects, level the roads, and plant more trees, then this problem can be eradicated. Look at the cleanliness of Dongjiaomin Lane, which is free of even a speck of dust. The reason for this can be imagined. Leveling roads requires a lot of money, which may not be possible overnight. As for planting trees, why can't it be done? In ancient times, the palace often planted locust and willow trees. Tang Dynasty poems depict this frequently. The Forbidden City in Beijing still retains the old rules. Today, beside the red walls from Zhonghua Gate to Tiananmen Gate, there are still many ancient locust trees. Their branches twist and turn, and their bark is mottled. Although they are scattered and not in rows, they can still provide beautiful shade. Besides this, there are also many locust and elm trees in front of the residences of princes and nobles. Mounds, altars, temples and shrines have many pine and cypress trees. On the sides of the imperial ditches, willows droop, lush and green, extending for several miles. All of this shows the abundance of trees in the past. During the years of the Republic of China, in the third and fourth years, municipal administration was promoted. Along the east and west Chang'an streets, weeping willows, German locusts and flowering cherries were planted. These two trees are easy to grow. Today, they provide shade during the long summer, complementing the yellow tiles and red walls, creating a beautiful scene. This shows that there were still talents in urban construction at that time. In recent years, every year during the Qingming Festival, countless saplings are purchased and planted in the streets. Since there is no one specifically responsible for irrigating and protecting them, they wither and die in less than ten days. Saplings are planted every year, and every year they end up with no trees. The same mistakes are repeated, and there is never a thorough plan for change. It is truly sad that there is no one in charge of Beijing's municipal authorities. Many of the newly opened roads and prosperous streets in recent years have no trees. Every summer, the scorching sun shines directly on them, causing pedestrians to be scorched from head to toe. Occasionally, one sees one or two young trees only shoulder-high, swaying as if they are about to die, in a very pitiful state. In fact, every year during tree planting, only ten specially assigned police officers need to be dispatched to patrol the entire city and supervise the matter. It is also possible to hold nearby residents responsible, with each household specifically protecting one tree. If it withers, they will be required to compensate. This is a simple task that is easy to accomplish. The fact that one can break a branch for an elder but does not do it is what describes the Beijing municipal authorities. There are many trees suitable for the soil in Beijing, such as the ailanthus and willow, which can grow almost anywhere. Without being cut down, they never die prematurely. Other trees such as mulberry, jujube, locust and elm can be used as offerings and firewood. Citizens regard them as ordinary. They can be widely planted. However, I believe that the tree that best represents Beijing is the flowering cherry, named for its resemblance to a horse's neck ornament. Its color is red above and white below. Its leaves are small and grow in pairs. It blooms during the day. It does not require cultivation. Without waiting ten years, it grows as tall as a building, and its dense shade can block the red dust. Its name and reality both match the description of an auspicious tree. If there were a wise municipal authority, they could spend a month planting this tree throughout the city, and its beautiful shade would last forever, and future generations would sing the praises of Zhaotang. The municipal government decided two years ago to make the chrysanthemum the city flower. However, the chrysanthemum is not unique to Beijing and is also the symbol of the Japanese imperial family, which is a confusing issue. Why not choose the flowering cherry and make it into a design, which would be more elegant and appropriate?

Rotary Club of Storytellers

A Husband's Wife (5) 176

— Jiang Hongjiao

Mrs. Li wanted to move Mr. Li with a very gentle and self-sacrificing method. She simply stood at the entrance of the alley to wait for her husband every night, but he remained indifferent and said nothing. One night, the northwest wind was as sharp as a razor, piercing the skin. Mrs. Li, wearing only a not-so-warm camel hair robe, still stood in front of the alley entrance, waiting for her husband. Suddenly, it started to snow. At first, it was just snowflakes, but later it snowed more and more heavily. Her whole body was covered in snow, turning her into a snowman. Her teeth were chattering from the cold. She leaned her body against the wall, hugging herself with her arms crossed. She forgot about sleep, forgot about the cold and pain, and only waited for her husband to come home. She knew the addresses of several of her husband's friends and could go to inquire, but she did not want his friends to know that he had been coming home so late recently, causing even the slightest damage to his reputation.

The gatekeeper was awakened from his sleep by the alarm clock. He hurriedly yawned, took the lock, and prepared to lock the alley gate. He discovered a person by the wall and was very pleased, thinking to exercise his authority. He thought that if it wasn't a petty thief, it was at least a beggar. He had the right to expel them, or scold them a few times, kick them, or arrest this person and send them to the police station. He could get the luck of being rewarded.

"Go away! What are you hiding here for?" The gatekeeper shouted in a rude and majestic Shandong accent, preparing to grab the person with his rough hands, similar to bear's paws.

"It's me, I'm from number eighty-eight." She was so frightened that she almost cried, but she calmed down and said this sentence.

"Oh? Such heavy snow, what are you doing? Go back quickly!" The gatekeeper changed to a gentler tone in disappointment, because he had discovered that the person standing there was not a petty thief or beggar, but Mrs. Li, who gave him a three-yuan tip every festival.

"No, I'm waiting for our husband."

"The wind is blowing so hard, the snow is falling so heavily, Mrs. Li, look! Your whole body is white, you should go back home and wait!"

"No, I'm waiting... for our... husband." She was partly because of the cold, and partly because she was saddened by what the gatekeeper said. She was resentful that her husband was not as good as an unrelated gatekeeper, who even said a word of concern.

No Major Changes in Financial Gold Standard 177

▲Slight Increase in Momentum: Yesterday, the fourth day, the gold standard showed a slight upward trend, with the situation being peaceful and without any special changes. From morning to night, it only fluctuated by four taels. Looking back, the net increase was two taels. However, the industry's intentions were hesitant, with both long and short positions making no effort. It seemed unmoved by the rise in the silver market. It was believed that the United States continued to sell gold, and with the stock market weak, the gold price opened high. However, there were always many open positions, leading to a downward trend. The exchange rate was stable and firm, so there was hope for an upward trend. However, there were fluctuations of two taels at times. The market was generally flat, fluctuating around seventy-seven taels. The foreign exchange rate remained stable. There was not much trading on the trading floor.

▲Morning Market Fluctuations: The October opening in the early morning rose by three taels to seven hundred and seventy-seven taels and six qian. Yarn Market in a Wait-and-See Stance 182

The yarn market is showing a very sluggish trend due to weak spot sales and the continued downturn in overseas cotton yarn conditions. The unfavorable environment has led to a lack of buyers, with both bulls and bears adopting a wait-and-see approach, awaiting changes before making a final decision.

▲ People's Standard Drags Downstream People's Standard

In the afternoon, bulls closed positions, leading to further drops of three, four, and five cents. The total transaction volume was 14,700 bales. Cotton Market: Initial Rise, Subsequent Fall 183

The cotton market initially rose but then fell. The weather is very unfavorable, with persistent rain. Consequently, most cotton merchants are leaning towards a bullish position, with particularly strong buying from the Hankou Huangbang and active purchases from the Huoji bang. This is entirely due to the poor domestic harvest. However, due to the surplus overseas and the weak trend of American cotton, speculators are aggressively selling, and the package volume is increasing. Given the overall situation, there is little prospect for American cotton to rise. However, considering the poor domestic cotton production, a price of around 34 taels for standard cotton may temporarily stabilize. Future movements will still depend on American cotton.

▲ Hankou Standard Fails to Improve

The Hankou Standard opened in the previous market with weak American cotton and poor sentiment. However, due to the unsettled rainy weather in the port, it initially rose by two to three cents. Later, large accounts sold off, causing it to fall back. The result was a rise of 1.5 cents, followed by a drop of one to two cents in the afternoon. The total transaction volume was 55,700 dan. A breakdown shows: Yuda sold 2,400 dan, Yongfeng 900 dan, Yichang 2,800 dan, Jifeng 1,200 dan, Taixing 1,100 dan; Shenchang bought 2,300 dan, Jifeng 1,200 dan, Dafu 1,900 dan, Xinheng 2,900 dan, Yuanda 2,000 dan. Taizhou Rice Sales are Brisk, Prices Rise 187

Yesterday, the imported rice market was stagnant as both local and outside customers showed no appetite. Futures prices rebounded slightly by two to three cents. 300 tons of 9-month small Jiaomi opened at 6.5 taels, and 100 tons of 10-month opened at 6.53 taels. The new trading market price was not favorable, and no transactions were made. Taizhou rice arrives daily, and the local market has a strong appetite. Supply cannot meet demand, and prices are rising steadily. Yesterday, another 3,500 bags of Taizhou white rice opened at a high of 13.23 yuan to 13 yuan, and 12.89 yuan.

Flour Market Greatly Affected by US Relief Wheat 188

Yesterday, the flour market opened down in both the morning and afternoon, with prices falling sharply across all months. The main driving factor was the official passage of the US relief wheat of 15 million bushels by the Central Political Council. This news was like a bolt from the blue for outsiders, and they were greatly shocked. The bullish sentiment in various months was overwhelmed. Mills did not greatly increase sales, so the market did not see a large drop. However, with this situation, the morale of the people is feared to be difficult to recover temporarily. As a result, the current month fell by 1.75 cents from the previous day, October and November fell by 2 cents, December fell by 2.5 cents, January fell by 2.75 cents, and February fell by 2.5 cents.

Wheat Futures Plummet Unceasingly 189

Yesterday, the wheat futures market plummeted in both the morning and afternoon. With the US wheat of 15 million bushels officially approved by the government, the food supply in the disaster areas should be maintained with surplus. Moreover, with the mills steadily releasing inventory, the abundance of wheat in the market should be known by all parties. A portion of inland groups, overwhelmed by this impact, could not resist and had to sell to close out positions. The lowest price for the current month fell to 3 taels and 8 mace 6 cents, October to 3 taels and 9 mace 4 cents, November to 3 taels and 9 mace 5 cents, December to 3 taels and 9 mace 9 cents, January to 4 taels and 3 cents, and February to 4 taels and 6 cents, a huge drop of 1 to 1.2 cents compared to the previous day's closing price. However, the closing was slightly better, with the current month down 8 cents, November down 9 cents, and December and February down 1 cent each.

Sugar Market: Raw and White Sugar Sold Off Actively 190

Yesterday, there were few reports from the sugar production area, and the market remained stable. Transactions on the guild market were still sparse. Dutch sugar, grade 24 raw white new cargo, was priced at 11 taels and 7 mace 5 cents; grade 20 medium white sugar, 11 taels and 2 mace, old cargo, 11 taels. The trend was fairly flat. Bowl Green sugar, with continued arrivals, saw slightly quieter demand, and the price fell to 8 taels 5 mace 5 cents to 5 cents. The market was generally stable. While Taikoo brand sugar's fixed price has risen by half a jiao, merchants showed little interest. Spot sugar was sluggish due to slow sales in various places, and the market reversed to flat. DY mark was priced at 11 taels 8 mace 2.5 cents to 8 cents; HM mark, 11 taels 4 mace 2.5 cents to 4 cents, slightly lower by 2.5 cents. B mark, 12 taels; CW mark, 11 taels 9 mace; HX mark, 11 taels 7 mace 5 cents, were still able to hold steady. Dutch sugar was actively sold off. Yesterday, Dachang Foreign Firm sold 200 tons of new grade raw white for October and November shipment at a price of 5 Dutch guilders and 7.5 cents. Huaxin Company sold 300 tons of old cargo, bagged white, for September and October shipment at 5 guilders and 7.25 cents. At the same time, Zhenxiang offered 5 guilders and 6.5 cents for old cargo, with strong buying interest, but the results are pending today's reply telegram.

Silk and Tea: Shuang Gong Native Silk Exempt from Inspection 191

However, exported Shuang Gong factory silk still requires inspection and measurement.

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce, in order to develop foreign trade and maintain reputation, requires all exported raw silk to undergo inspection and measurement, which is implemented by the Silk Inspection Office of the Commodity Inspection Bureau. It is now known that Shuang Gong native silk used by domestic silk factories has been explicitly exempted from inspection. However, exported Shuang Gong factory silk still requires inspection and measurement. Yesterday, the ministry ordered the Shanghai Silk Factory Association to notify the Shuang Gong silk factories to take note.

Core-Picked Zhen Mei Sells Well in Europe 192

Yesterday, the tea market in this port saw continued strong interest from foreign firms in core-picked Zhen Mei from Wuyuan and Tunxi. Firms such as Yingzhuang, Xiehe, Yihuo, Jinlong, and Tongfu were very active. The market situation is becoming more active, and tea prices are rising across the board. Sentiment is extremely strong. According to a telegram from Morocco, the inventory of green tea is gradually dwindling, and the autumn sales season has begun. It is expected that the market will continue to develop.

Foreign Firms' Silk Sales Remain Clear and Firm 193

Yesterday, the silk market continued to be clear. New York's silk market saw prices for Chinese silk not high, English and French needs for yellow and white silk though prices were not high, and price transfer was difficult. Yesterday, Shenyu and other companies took in 20 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, and Xinfu took in 20 bales of Sichuan yellow factory silk. Xinchang took in 10 bales of white Gan silk, and the prices remained firm.

Pi Tou, Wide/Tight Camel Down Sell Well in a Timely Manner 194

Wide and tight camel down have been selling well recently, with continued interest from local customers. Since the domestic factory products have been available, foreign goods have been greatly impacted. Currently, the wide and tight camel down are on the market, and sales are very active. In previous years, imported goods were often sold off early and quickly. Now, they are largely absent. The domestic camel down from our factory, with the oldest and most established brand, Weiyi, is the first inventor. The best quality is Weilin's Tiger pattern. The Tiger pattern stripe camel down sells for 2 taels and 3 mace per yard wholesale, and the plain color is 1 tael and 7 mace and 2.5 cents. Other brands such as Weiyi's Double Deer pattern, Tianxiang's Crane pattern, Xianda's Camel brand, Shengda's Dragon and Phoenix, and Mingfa's Huadong are all sold at 2 taels and 2 mace and 5 cents, including commission, and plain colors at 1 tael and 7 mace, including commission. However, these are all limited to delivery within Shanghai. For customs declaration and transportation to other places, an additional 1 mace of silver per yard is required.

▲ Small-Sized Nails: Condition Deteriorating
